<p><b>São Paulo</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/aʊ/: 'ou' in 'mouth'">aʊ</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/aʊ/: 'ou' in 'mouth'">aʊ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span style="font-size:85%;">Portuguese: </span><span class="IPA" lang="pt-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[sɐ̃w̃ ˈpawlu]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Br-SaoPaulo.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/27/Br-SaoPaulo.ogg" title="Br-SaoPaulo.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; Portuguese for '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Paul" title="Saint Paul">Saint Paul</a>') is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_in_Brazil" title="List of largest cities in Brazil">most populous city</a> in Brazil, and is the capital of the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">state of São Paulo</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Brazilian_states_by_population" title="List of Brazilian states by population">most populous</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Brazilian_federative_units_by_gross_domestic_product" title="List of Brazilian federative units by gross domestic product">wealthiest</a> Brazilian state, located in the country's <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Region,_Brazil" title="Southeast Region, Brazil">Southeast Region</a>. Listed by the <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">GaWC</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">alpha global city</a>, São Paulo is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_Americas_by_population" title="List of cities in the Americas by population">most populous city proper in the Americas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>, as well as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_proper_by_population" title="List of cities proper by population">world's 4th largest city proper by population</a>. Additionally, São Paulo is the largest <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese-speaking</a> city in the world. It exerts strong international influences in commerce, finance, arts and entertainment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The city's name honors <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">the Apostle, Saint Paul of Tarsus</a>. The city's <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater São Paulo">Greater São Paulo</a>, ranks as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Brazil" title="List of metropolitan areas in Brazil">most populous in Brazil</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_by_population" title="List of metropolitan areas by population">12th most populous on Earth</a>. The process of <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbation</a> between the metropolitan areas around the Greater São Paulo (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Region_of_Campinas" title="Metropolitan Region of Campinas">Campinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baixada_Santista" title="Baixada Santista">Santos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jundia%C3%AD" title="Jundiaí">Jundiaí</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Region_of_Sorocaba" title="Metropolitan Region of Sorocaba">Sorocaba</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Region_of_Vale_do_Para%C3%ADba_e_Litoral_Norte" title="Metropolitan Region of Vale do Paraíba e Litoral Norte">São José dos Campos</a>) created the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Macrometropolis" title="São Paulo Macrometropolis">São Paulo Macrometropolis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megalopolis_(city_type)" title="Megalopolis (city type)">megalopolis</a> with more than 30 million inhabitants, one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities" title="List of largest cities">most populous urban agglomerations in the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Megalópole_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Megalópole-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Having the largest economy by <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> the city is home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BM%26F_Bovespa" title="BM&amp;F Bovespa">São Paulo Stock Exchange</a>. <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">Paulista Avenue</a> is the economic core of São Paulo. The city has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">23rd largest GDP in the world</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> representing alone 10.7% of all <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil" title="Economy of Brazil">Brazilian GDP</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and 36% of the production of goods and services in the state of São Paulo, being home to 63% of established <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinationals</a> in Brazil,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> and was responsible for 28% of the national scientific production in 2005, as measured by the number of science papers published in journals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>The metropolis is also home to several of <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Brazil" title="List of tallest buildings in Brazil">the tallest skyscrapers in Brazil</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Mirante_do_Vale" title="Mirante do Vale">Mirante do Vale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edif%C3%ADcio_It%C3%A1lia" title="Edifício Itália">Edifício Itália</a>, <a href="/wiki/Altino_Arantes_Building" title="Altino Arantes Building">Banespa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Centro_Empresarial_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_Unidas" title="Centro Empresarial Nações Unidas">North Tower</a> and many others. The city has cultural, economic and political influence nationally and internationally. It is home to monuments, parks and museums such as the <a href="/wiki/Latin_America_Memorial" title="Latin America Memorial">Latin American Memorial</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ibirapuera_Park" title="Ibirapuera Park">Ibirapuera Park</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museu_Paulista" title="Museu Paulista">Museum of Ipiranga</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Museum_of_Art" title="São Paulo Museum of Art">São Paulo Museum of Art</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Museum of the Portuguese Language">Museum of the Portuguese Language</a>. The city holds events like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sao_Paulo_Jazz_Festival" title="Sao Paulo Jazz Festival">São Paulo Jazz Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Art_Biennial" title="São Paulo Art Biennial">São Paulo Art Biennial</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="Brazilian Grand Prix">Brazilian Grand Prix</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Fashion_Week" title="São Paulo Fashion Week">São Paulo Fashion Week</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brasil_Open" title="Brasil Open">ATP Brasil Open</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brasil_Game_Show" title="Brasil Game Show">Brasil Game Show</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comic_Con_Experience" title="Comic Con Experience">Comic Con Experience</a>. <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Gay_Pride_Parade" title="São Paulo Gay Pride Parade">São Paulo's LGBT Pride parade</a> ranks <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_LGBT_events" title="List of largest LGBT events">second only</a> to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> <a href="/wiki/NYC_Pride_March" title="NYC Pride March">Pride March</a> as the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_pride" title="Gay pride">LGBTQ pride</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pride_march" title="Pride march">parade</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCWorld'sLargestPrideParade_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYCWorld'sLargestPrideParade-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCWorld_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYCWorld-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>São Paulo is a <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">cosmopolitan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melting_pot" title="Melting pot">melting pot</a> city, home to the largest <a href="/wiki/Arab_Brazilians" title="Arab Brazilians">Arab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilians" title="Italian Brazilians">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilians" title="Japanese Brazilians">Japanese</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_Brazilian" title="Portuguese Brazilian">Portuguese</a> diasporas, with examples including <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_enclave" title="Ethnic enclave">ethnic neighborhoods</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bixiga" title="Bixiga">Bixiga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bom_Retiro_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Bom Retiro (district of São Paulo)">Bom Retiro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Liberdade_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Liberdade (district of São Paulo)">Liberdade</a>. In 2016, inhabitants of the city were native to over 200 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Imigrantes2016_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Imigrantes2016-17">[17]</a></sup> People from the city are known as <i>paulistanos</i>, while <i>paulistas</i> designates anyone from <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">the state</a>, including the <i>paulistanos</i>. The city's <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> motto, which it has shared with <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_battleship_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Brazilian battleship São Paulo">the battleship</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_aircraft_carrier_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(A12)" title="Brazilian aircraft carrier São Paulo (A12)">the aircraft carrier</a> named after it, is <i>Non ducor, duco</i>, which translates as "I am not led, I lead."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The city, which is also colloquially known as <i>Sampa</i> or <i>Terra da Garoa</i> (Land of Drizzle), is known for its unreliable weather, the size of its helicopter fleet, its architecture, gastronomy, severe traffic congestion and <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="List of tallest buildings in São Paulo">skyscrapers</a>. São Paulo was one of the host cities of the <a href="/wiki/1950_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1950 FIFA World Cup">1950</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>. Additionally, the city hosted the <a href="/wiki/1963_Pan_American_Games" title="1963 Pan American Games">IV Pan American Games</a> and the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Indy_300" title="São Paulo Indy 300">São Paulo Indy 300</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a chronological guide, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Timeline of São Paulo">Timeline of São Paulo</a>.</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Indigenous_Period">Early Indigenous Period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early Indigenous Period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1062260506">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:20em; ; font-size: 90%; background-color: #B0C4DE;">
<div class="quotebox-title" style="background-color: #B0C4DE;">Historical affiliations</div>
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal"><img alt="Portugal" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_Portugal_%281640%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Portugal_%281640%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_Portugal_%281640%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Portugal_%281640%29.svg.png 1.5x, title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> 1554–1815<br/><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="716" data-file-width="957" decoding="async" height="15" 2x" width="20"/></span> <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a>  1815–1822<br/><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="638" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_Brazil_%281822%E2%80%931870%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Brazil_%281822%E2%80%931870%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_Brazil_%281822%E2%80%931870%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Brazil_%281822%E2%80%931870%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Flag_of_Brazil_%281822%E2%80%931870%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Brazil_%281822%E2%80%931870%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a> 1822–1889<br/><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil"><img alt="Brazil" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/22px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/33px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/43px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 2x" width="22"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Republic of Brazil</a> 1889–present
</p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<p>The region of modern-day São Paulo, then known as Piratininga plains around the <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_River" title="Tietê River">Tietê River</a>, was inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Tupi_people" title="Tupi people">Tupi people</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Tupiniquim" title="Tupiniquim">Tupiniquim</a>, Guaianás, and <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaraní people">Guarani</a>. Other tribes also lived in areas that today form the metropolitan region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>The region was divided in Caciquedoms (chiefdoms) at the time of encounter with the Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The most notable <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacique</a> was <a href="/wiki/Tibiri%C3%A7%C3%A1" title="Tibiriçá">Tibiriçá</a>, known for his support for the Portuguese and other European colonists. Among the many indigenous names of places, rivers, neighborhoods, etc., that survive today are <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Tietê, São Paulo">Tietê</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ipiranga_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Ipiranga (district of São Paulo)">Ipiranga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamanduate%C3%AD_River" title="Tamanduateí River">Tamanduateí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vale_do_Anhangaba%C3%BA" title="Vale do Anhangabaú">Anhangabaú</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piratininga" title="Piratininga">Piratininga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Itaquaquecetuba" title="Itaquaquecetuba">Itaquaquecetuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotia" title="Cotia">Cotia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Itapevi" title="Itapevi">Itapevi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barueri" title="Barueri">Barueri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Embu-Gua%C3%A7u" title="Embu-Guaçu">Embu-Guaçu</a>, etc.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period">Colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_1909.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1120" data-file-width="1598" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1909.jpg/220px-Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1909.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1909.jpg/330px-Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1909.jpg/440px-Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_1909.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva_-_Funda%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_1909.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Founding of São Paulo</i>, 1909 painting by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Pereira_da_Silva" title="Oscar Pereira da Silva">Oscar Pereira da Silva</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3953" data-file-width="7940" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/220px-P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/330px-P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/440px-P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Courtyard of the College, <i>Pátio do Colégio</i>, in the Historic Center of São Paulo. At this location, the city was founded in 1554. The current building is a reconstruction made in the late 20th century, based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">Jesuit</a> <a href="/wiki/College" title="College">college</a> and <a href="/wiki/Church_(building)" title="Church (building)">church</a> that were erected at the site in 1653</div></div></div>
<p>The Portuguese village of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_dos_Campos_de_Piratininga" title="São Paulo dos Campos de Piratininga">São Paulo dos Campos de Piratininga</a> was marked by the founding of the <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1tio_do_Col%C3%A9gio" title="Pátio do Colégio">Colégio de São Paulo de Piratininga</a> on 25 January 1554. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> college of twelve priests included <a href="/wiki/Manuel_da_N%C3%B3brega" title="Manuel da Nóbrega">Manuel da Nóbrega</a> and Spanish priest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Anchieta" title="José de Anchieta">José de Anchieta</a>. They built a mission on top of a steep hill between the <a href="/wiki/Anhangaba%C3%BA_River" title="Anhangabaú River">Anhangabaú</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tamanduate%C3%AD_River" title="Tamanduateí River">Tamanduateí</a> rivers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lawrence183_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lawrence183-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>They first had a small structure built of <a href="/wiki/Rammed_earth" title="Rammed earth">rammed earth</a>, made by Native Indian workers in their traditional style. The priests wanted to <a href="/wiki/Catechesis" title="Catechesis">evangelize</a> these Indians who lived in the Plateau region of Piratininga and convert them to Christianity. The site was separated from the coast by the <a href="/wiki/Serra_do_Mar" title="Serra do Mar">Serra do Mar</a> mountain range, called "Serra Paranapiacaba” by the Indians.
</p><p>The college was named for a Christian saint and its founding on the feast day of the celebration of the conversion of the Apostle <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_of_Tarsus" title="Paul of Tarsus">Paul of Tarsus</a>. Father José de Anchieta wrote this account in a letter to the Society of Jesus:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The settlement of the region's Courtyard of the College began in 1560. During the visit of <a href="/wiki/Mem_de_S%C3%A1" title="Mem de Sá">Mem de Sá</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors-general_of_Brazil" title="List of governors-general of Brazil">Governor-General of Brazil</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_of_S%C3%A3o_Vicente" title="Captaincy of São Vicente">Captaincy of São Vicente</a>, he ordered the transfer of the population of the Village of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Bernardo_do_Campo" title="São Bernardo do Campo">São Bernardo do Campo</a> to the vicinity of the college. It was then named "College of St. Paul Piratininga". The new location was on a steep hill adjacent to a large wetland, the Várzea do Carmo. It offered better protection from attacks by local Indian groups. It was renamed Vila de São Paulo, belonging to the Captaincy of São Vicente.</p></blockquote>
<p>For the next two centuries, São Paulo developed as a poor and isolated village that survived largely through the cultivation of <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence crops</a> by the labor of natives. For a long time, São Paulo was the only village in Brazil's interior, as travel was too difficult for many to reach the area. Mem de Sá forbade colonists to use the Caminho do Piraiquê <i>(Piraiquê Path)</i> and today known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pia%C3%A7aguera" title="Piaçaguera">Piaçaguera</a>, because of frequent Indian raids along it.
</p><p>On 22 March 1681, Luís Álvares de Castro, the Second Marquis de Cascais and donee of the Captaincy of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Vicente, São Paulo">São Vicente</a>, moved the capital to the village of São Paulo <i>(see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Timeline of São Paulo">Timeline of São Paulo</a>)</i>, designating it the "Head of the captaincy". The new capital was established on 23 April 1683, with public celebrations.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bandeirantes">The Bandeirantes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Bandeirantes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bandeirantes" title="Bandeirantes">Bandeirantes</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_-_Monumento_%C3%A0s_Bandeiras_-_foto_Carlos_Alkmin_nr_07-13_4282b.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Sao_Paulo_-_Monumento_%C3%A0s_Bandeiras_-_foto_Carlos_Alkmin_nr_07-13_4282b.jpg/220px-Sao_Paulo_-_Monumento_%C3%A0s_Bandeiras_-_foto_Carlos_Alkmin_nr_07-13_4282b.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Sao_Paulo_-_Monumento_%C3%A0s_Bandeiras_-_foto_Carlos_Alkmin_nr_07-13_4282b.jpg/330px-Sao_Paulo_-_Monumento_%C3%A0s_Bandeiras_-_foto_Carlos_Alkmin_nr_07-13_4282b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Sao_Paulo_-_Monumento_%C3%A0s_Bandeiras_-_foto_Carlos_Alkmin_nr_07-13_4282b.jpg/440px-Sao_Paulo_-_Monumento_%C3%A0s_Bandeiras_-_foto_Carlos_Alkmin_nr_07-13_4282b.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_-_Monumento_%C3%A0s_Bandeiras_-_foto_Carlos_Alkmin_nr_07-13_4282b.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Monument_to_the_Bandeiras" title="Monument to the Bandeiras">Monument to the Bandeiras</a> commemorates the 17th-century <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bandeiras" title="Bandeiras">bandeiras</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>In the 17th century, São Paulo was one of the poorest regions of the Portuguese colony. It was also the center of interior colonial development. Because they were extremely poor, the Paulistas could not afford to buy <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slaves</a>, as did other Portuguese colonists. The discovery of gold in the region of <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a>, in the 1690s, brought attention and new settlers to São Paulo. The Captaincy of São Paulo and Minas de Ouro (see <a href="/wiki/Captaincies_of_Brazil" title="Captaincies of Brazil">Captaincies of Brazil</a>) was created on 3 November 1709, when the Portuguese crown purchased the Captaincies of São Paulo and Santo Amaro from the former grantees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Conveniently located in the country, up the steep <i><a href="/wiki/Serra_do_Mar" title="Serra do Mar">Serra do Mar</a></i> escarpment/mountain range when traveling from <a href="/wiki/Santos,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Santos, São Paulo">Santos</a>, while also not too far from the coastline, São Paulo became a safe place to stay for tired travelers. The town became a center for the <i><a href="/wiki/Bandeirantes" title="Bandeirantes">bandeirantes</a></i>, intrepid invaders who marched into unknown lands in search for gold, diamonds, precious stones, and Indians to enslave. The <i>bandeirantes</i>, which could be translated as "flag-bearers" or "flag-followers", organized excursions into the land with the primary purpose of profit and the expansion of territory for the Portuguese crown. Trade grew from the local markets and from providing food and accommodation for explorers. The <i>bandeirantes</i> eventually became politically powerful as a group, and forced the expulsion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">Jesuits</a> from the city of São Paulo in 1640. The two groups had frequently come into conflict because of the Jesuits' opposition to the domestic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a> in Indians.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Entrada_Leste_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_em_1821.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2798" data-file-width="4013" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Entrada_Leste_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_em_1821.jpg/220px-Entrada_Leste_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_em_1821.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Entrada_Leste_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_em_1821.jpg/330px-Entrada_Leste_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_em_1821.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Entrada_Leste_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_em_1821.jpg/440px-Entrada_Leste_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_em_1821.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Entrada_Leste_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_em_1821.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>East entrance of the city of São Paulo in 1821, by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Arnaud_Julien_Palli%C3%A8re&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Arnaud Julien Pallière (page does not exist)">Arnaud Julien Pallière</a> (1784-1862).</div></div></div>
<p>On 11 July 1711, the town of São Paulo was elevated to city status. Around the 1720s, gold was found by the pioneers in the regions near what are now <a href="/wiki/Cuiab%C3%A1" title="Cuiabá">Cuiabá</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goi%C3%A2nia" title="Goiânia">Goiânia</a>. The Portuguese expanded their Brazilian territory beyond the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tordesillas_Line" title="Tordesillas Line">Tordesillas Line</a> to incorporate the gold regions. When the gold ran out in the late 18th century, São Paulo shifted to growing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a>. Cultivation of this commodity crop spread through the interior of the Captaincy. The sugar was exported through the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Santos" title="Port of Santos">Port of Santos</a>. At that time, the first modern highway between São Paulo and the coast was constructed and named the Calçada do Lorena <i>("Lorena’s <a href="/wiki/Sett_(paving)" title="Sett (paving)">settway</a>")</i>. Nowadays, the estate that is home to the Governor of the State of São Paulo, in the city of São Paulo, is called the <i><a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Bandeirantes" title="Palácio dos Bandeirantes">Palácio dos Bandeirantes</a></i> (Bandeirantes Palace), in the neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Morumbi,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Morumbi, São Paulo">Morumbi</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_Period">Imperial Period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Imperial Period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vista_a%C3%A9rea_do_Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2976" data-file-width="3968" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Vista_a%C3%A9rea_do_Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia.jpg/220px-Vista_a%C3%A9rea_do_Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Vista_a%C3%A9rea_do_Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia.jpg/330px-Vista_a%C3%A9rea_do_Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Vista_a%C3%A9rea_do_Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia.jpg/440px-Vista_a%C3%A9rea_do_Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vista_a%C3%A9rea_do_Monumento_%C3%A0_Independ%C3%AAncia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Monument_to_the_Independence_of_Brazil" title="Monument to the Independence of Brazil">Monument to Independence</a> in Independence Park, located at the place where then-<a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Prince Pedro</a> proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">independence of Brazil</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marc_Ferrez_-_IMS_002001MF005003.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="5280" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Marc_Ferrez_-_IMS_002001MF005003.jpg/220px-Marc_Ferrez_-_IMS_002001MF005003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Marc_Ferrez_-_IMS_002001MF005003.jpg/330px-Marc_Ferrez_-_IMS_002001MF005003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Marc_Ferrez_-_IMS_002001MF005003.jpg/440px-Marc_Ferrez_-_IMS_002001MF005003.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marc_Ferrez_-_IMS_002001MF005003.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pra%C3%A7a_da_S%C3%A9" title="Praça da Sé">Cathedral Square of São Paulo</a> in 1880, during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Emperor Pedro II</a> by <a href="/wiki/Marc_Ferrez_(photographer)" title="Marc Ferrez (photographer)">Marc Ferrez</a></div></div></div>
<p>After Brazil became <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">independent from Portugal</a> in 1822, as declared by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Emperor Pedro I</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Monument_to_the_Independence_of_Brazil" title="Monument to the Independence of Brazil">Monument to the Independence of Brazil</a> is located, he named São Paulo as an Imperial City. In 1827, a law school was founded at the Convent of São Francisco, today part of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="University of São Paulo">University of São Paulo</a>. The influx of students and teachers gave a new impetus to the city's growth, thanks to which the city became the <i>Imperial City and Borough of Students of St. Paul of Piratininga</i>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Coffee_cycle" title="Coffee cycle">expansion of coffee production</a> was a major factor in the growth of São Paulo, as it became the region's chief export crop and yielded good revenue. It was cultivated initially in the <a href="/wiki/Para%C3%ADba_Valley" title="Paraíba Valley">Paraíba Valley</a> region in the East of the State of São Paulo, and later on in the regions of <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">Campinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Claro,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Rio Claro, São Paulo">Rio Claro</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Carlos" title="São Carlos">São Carlos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ribeir%C3%A3o_Preto" title="Ribeirão Preto">Ribeirão Preto</a>.
</p><p>From 1869 onward, São Paulo was connected to the port of Santos by the <a href="/wiki/Estrada_de_Ferro_Santos-Jundia%C3%AD" title="Estrada de Ferro Santos-Jundiaí">Estrada de Ferro Santos-Jundiaí</a> (Santos-Jundiaí Railroad), nicknamed<i> The Lady</i>. In the late 19th century, several other railroads connected the interior to the state capital. São Paulo became the point of convergence of all railroads from the interior of the state. Coffee was the economic engine for major economic and population growth in the State of São Paulo.
</p><p>In 1888, the "Golden Law" (<i><a href="/wiki/Lei_%C3%81urea" title="Lei Áurea">Lei Áurea</a></i>) was sanctioned by <a href="/wiki/Isabel,_Princess_Imperial_of_Brazil" title="Isabel, Princess Imperial of Brazil">Isabel, Princess Imperial of Brazil</a>, 
abolishing the institution of slavery in Brazil. Slaves were the main source of labor in the coffee plantations until then. As a consequence of this law, and following governmental stimulus towards the increase of immigration, the province began to receive a large number of immigrants, largely Italians, Japanese and Portuguese peasants, many of whom settled in the capital. The region's first industries also began to emerge, providing jobs to the newcomers, especially those who had to learn Portuguese.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Republican_Period">Old Republican Period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Old Republican Period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guilherme_Gaensly_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz,_c._1900.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Guilherme_Gaensly_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz%2C_c._1900.jpg/220px-Guilherme_Gaensly_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz%2C_c._1900.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Guilherme_Gaensly_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz%2C_c._1900.jpg/330px-Guilherme_Gaensly_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz%2C_c._1900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Guilherme_Gaensly_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz%2C_c._1900.jpg/440px-Guilherme_Gaensly_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz%2C_c._1900.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guilherme_Gaensly_-_Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz,_c._1900.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Luz_Station" title="Luz Station">Luz Station</a> in 1900</div></div></div>
<p>By the time Brazil became a republic on 15 November 1889, coffee exports were still an important part of São Paulo's economy. São Paulo grew strong in the national political scene, taking turns with the also rich state of Minas Gerais in electing <a href="/wiki/List_of_presidents_of_Brazil" title="List of presidents of Brazil">Brazilian presidents</a>, an alliance that became known as "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_com_leite_politics" title="Café com leite politics">coffee and milk</a>", given that <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a> was famous for its dairy production. During this period, São Paulo went from regional center to national metropolis, becoming industrialized and reaching its first million inhabitants in 1928. Its greatest growth in this period was relative in the 1890s when it doubled its population. The height of the coffee period is represented by the construction of the second <a href="/wiki/Luz_Station" title="Luz Station">Luz Station</a> (the present building) at the end of the 19th century and by the <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">Paulista Avenue</a> in 1900, where they built many mansions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prefeitura_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prefeitura-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>Industrialization was the economic cycle that followed the coffee plantation model. By the hands of some industrious families, including many immigrants of Italian and Jewish origin, factories began to arise and São Paulo became known for its smoky, foggy air. The cultural scene followed <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">modernist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naturalism_(philosophy)" title="Naturalism (philosophy)">naturalist</a> tendencies in fashion at the beginning of the 20th century. Some examples of notable modernist artists are poets <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade" title="Mário de Andrade">Mário de Andrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oswald_de_Andrade" title="Oswald de Andrade">Oswald de Andrade</a>, artists <a href="/wiki/Anita_Malfatti" title="Anita Malfatti">Anita Malfatti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tarsila_do_Amaral" title="Tarsila do Amaral">Tarsila do Amaral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lasar_Segall" title="Lasar Segall">Lasar Segall</a>, and sculptor <a href="/wiki/Victor_Brecheret" title="Victor Brecheret">Victor Brecheret</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Modern_Art_Week" title="Modern Art Week">Modern Art Week</a> of 1922 that took place at the <a href="/wiki/Theatro_Municipal_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Theatro Municipal (São Paulo)">Theatro Municipal</a> was an event marked by <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> ideas and works of art. In 1929, São Paulo won its first skyscraper, the <a href="/wiki/Martinelli_Building" title="Martinelli Building">Martinelli Building</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prefeitura_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Prefeitura-23">[23]</a></sup> The modifications made in the city by Antônio da Silva Prado, Baron of Duprat and <a href="/wiki/Washington_Lu%C3%ADs" title="Washington Luís">Washington Luís</a>, who governed from 1899 to 1919, contributed to the climate development of the city; some scholars consider that the entire city was demolished and rebuilt at that time. São Paulo's main economic activities derive from the services industry – factories are since long gone, and in came financial services institutions, law firms, consulting firms. Old factory buildings and warehouses still dot the landscape in neighborhoods such as <a href="/wiki/Barra_Funda" title="Barra Funda">Barra Funda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%A1s" title="Brás">Brás</a>. Some cities around São Paulo, such as <a href="/wiki/Diadema,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Diadema, São Paulo">Diadema</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Bernardo_do_Campo" title="São Bernardo do Campo">São Bernardo do Campo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santo_Andr%C3%A9" title="Santo André">Santo André</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cubat%C3%A3o" title="Cubatão">Cubatão</a> are still heavily industrialized to the present day, with factories producing from cosmetics to chemicals to automobiles.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Image001_Anhangabau.jpg" title="Anhangabaú Valley in Downtown São Paulo, 1925"><img alt="" data-file-height="1056" data-file-width="2961" decoding="async" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Image001_Anhangabau.jpg/800px-Image001_Anhangabau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Image001_Anhangabau.jpg/1200px-Image001_Anhangabau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Image001_Anhangabau.jpg/1600px-Image001_Anhangabau.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Image001_Anhangabau.jpg" title="File:Image001 Anhangabau.jpg"> </a></div><a href="/wiki/Vale_do_Anhangaba%C3%BA" title="Vale do Anhangabaú">Anhangabaú Valley</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Zone_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Central Zone of São Paulo">Downtown São Paulo</a>, 1925</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutionalist_Revolution_of_1932">Constitutionalist Revolution of 1932</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Constitutionalist Revolution of 1932">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Constitutionalist_Revolution" title="Constitutionalist Revolution">Constitutionalist Revolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A3o_Paulo_aviation_group_in_Campo_de_Marte_September_1932.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="372" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_aviation_group_in_Campo_de_Marte_September_1932.jpg/220px-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_aviation_group_in_Campo_de_Marte_September_1932.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_aviation_group_in_Campo_de_Marte_September_1932.jpg/330px-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_aviation_group_in_Campo_de_Marte_September_1932.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_aviation_group_in_Campo_de_Marte_September_1932.jpg/440px-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_aviation_group_in_Campo_de_Marte_September_1932.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A3o_Paulo_aviation_group_in_Campo_de_Marte_September_1932.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Group of aviators from São Paulo at <a href="/wiki/Campo_de_Marte_Airport" title="Campo de Marte Airport">Campo de Marte Airport</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Constitutionalist_Revolution" title="Constitutionalist Revolution">Constitutionalist Revolution</a></div></div></div>
<p>This revolution is considered by some historians as the last armed conflict to take place in Brazil's history. On 9 July 1932, the population of São Paulo town rose against a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> by <a href="/wiki/Get%C3%BAlio_Vargas" title="Getúlio Vargas">Getúlio Vargas</a> to take the presidential office. The movement grew out of local resentment from the fact that Vargas ruled by decree, unbound by a constitution, in a provisional government. The 1930 coup also affected São Paulo by eroding the autonomy that states enjoyed during the term of the 1891 Constitution and preventing the inauguration of the governor of São Paulo <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BAlio_Prestes" title="Júlio Prestes">Júlio Prestes</a> in the Presidency of the Republic, while simultaneously overthrowing President <a href="/wiki/Washington_Lu%C3%ADs" title="Washington Luís">Washington Luís</a>, who was governor of São Paulo from 1920 to 1924. These events marked the end of the <a href="/wiki/First_Brazilian_Republic" title="First Brazilian Republic">Old Republic</a>.
</p><p>The uprising commenced on 9 July 1932, after four protesting students were killed by federal government troops on 23 May 1932. On the wake of their deaths, a movement called <a href="/wiki/MMDC" title="MMDC">MMDC</a> (from the initials of the names of each of the four students killed, Martins, Miragaia, Dráusio and Camargo) started. A fifth victim, Alvarenga, was also shot that night, but died months later. In a few months, the state of São Paulo rebelled against the federal government. Counting on the solidarity of the political elites of two other powerful states, (<a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a>), the politicians from São Paulo expected a quick war. However, that solidarity was never translated into actual support, and the São Paulo revolt was militarily crushed on 2 October 1932. In total, there were 87 days of fighting (9 July to 4 October 1932 – with the last two days after the surrender of São Paulo), with a balance of 934 official deaths, though non-official estimates report up to 2,200 dead, and many cities in the state of São Paulo suffered damage due to fighting. There is an <a href="/wiki/Obelisk_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Obelisk of São Paulo">obelisk</a> in front of <a href="/wiki/Ibirapuera_Park" title="Ibirapuera Park">Ibirapuera Park</a> that serves as a memorial to the young men that died for the MMDC. The <a href="/wiki/Law_School,_University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Law School, University of São Paulo">University of São Paulo's Law School</a> also pays homage to the students that died during this period with plaques hung on its arcades.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:17-08-2008_003Pico_do_Jaragu%C3%A1_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo(By_Felipe_Mostarda).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1363" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/17-08-2008_003Pico_do_Jaragu%C3%A1_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%28By_Felipe_Mostarda%29.JPG/220px-17-08-2008_003Pico_do_Jaragu%C3%A1_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%28By_Felipe_Mostarda%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/17-08-2008_003Pico_do_Jaragu%C3%A1_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%28By_Felipe_Mostarda%29.JPG/330px-17-08-2008_003Pico_do_Jaragu%C3%A1_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%28By_Felipe_Mostarda%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/17-08-2008_003Pico_do_Jaragu%C3%A1_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%28By_Felipe_Mostarda%29.JPG/440px-17-08-2008_003Pico_do_Jaragu%C3%A1_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%28By_Felipe_Mostarda%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:17-08-2008_003Pico_do_Jaragu%C3%A1_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo(By_Felipe_Mostarda).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pico_do_Jaragu%C3%A1" title="Pico do Jaraguá">Jaraguá Peak</a> is the highest point in the city, at 1,135 meters (3,724 ft)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>São Paulo is the capital of the most populous state in Brazil, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo</a>, located at <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> 23°33'01'' south and <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a> 46°38'02'' west. The total area of the municipality is 1,521.11 square kilometres (587.30 sq mi), according to the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics</a> (IBGE), being the ninth largest in the state in terms of territorial extension.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBGE_SãoPaulo_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-IBGE_SãoPaulo-25">[25]</a></sup> Of the entire area of the municipality, 949,611 square kilometres (366,647 sq mi) are urban areas (2015), being the largest urban area in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMBRAPA-2015_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-EMBRAPA-2015-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>The city is on a <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateau</a> placed beyond the <a href="/wiki/Serra_do_Mar" title="Serra do Mar">Serra do Mar</a> (Portuguese for "Sea Range" or "Coastal Range"), itself a component of the vast region known as the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Highlands" title="Brazilian Highlands">Brazilian Highlands</a>, with an average elevation of around 799 meters (2,621 ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>, although being at a distance of only about 70 kilometers (43 mi) from <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">the Atlantic Ocean</a>. The distance is covered by two highways, the <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Anchieta" title="Rodovia Anchieta">Anchieta</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_dos_Imigrantes" title="Rodovia dos Imigrantes">Imigrantes</a>, (see "<a href="#Transportation">Transportation</a>" below) that roll down the range, leading to the port city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santos,_Brazil" title="Santos, Brazil">Santos</a> and the beach resort of <a href="/wiki/Guaruj%C3%A1" title="Guarujá">Guarujá</a>. Rolling terrain prevails within the urbanized areas of São Paulo except in its northern area, where the <a href="/wiki/Serra_da_Cantareira" title="Serra da Cantareira">Serra da Cantareira</a> Range reaches a higher elevation and a sizable remnant of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Forest" title="Atlantic Forest">Atlantic Rain Forest</a>. The region is seismically stable and no significant <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">activity</a> has ever been recorded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrography">Hydrography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Hydrography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Water_management_in_the_Metropolitan_Region_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Water management in the Metropolitan Region of São Paulo">Water management in the Metropolitan Region of São Paulo</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:402px;max-width:402px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:205px;max-width:205px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:127px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marginal_tiet%C3%AA.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2203" data-file-width="3504" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Marginal_tiet%C3%AA.jpg/203px-Marginal_tiet%C3%AA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Marginal_tiet%C3%AA.jpg/305px-Marginal_tiet%C3%AA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Marginal_tiet%C3%AA.jpg/406px-Marginal_tiet%C3%AA.jpg 2x" width="203"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_River" title="Tietê River">Tietê River</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Marginal_Tiet%C3%AA" title="Marginal Tietê">Marginal Tietê</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:193px;max-width:193px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:127px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Billings_2008051703.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Billings_2008051703.jpg/191px-Billings_2008051703.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Billings_2008051703.jpg/287px-Billings_2008051703.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Billings_2008051703.jpg/382px-Billings_2008051703.jpg 2x" width="191"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Billings_Reservoir" title="Billings Reservoir">Billings Reservoir</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_River" title="Tietê River">Tietê River</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributary</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pinheiros_River" title="Pinheiros River">Pinheiros River</a>, were once important sources of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freshwater" title="Freshwater">fresh water</a> and leisure for São Paulo. However, heavy industrial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Effluents" title="Effluents">effluents</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wastewater" title="Wastewater">wastewater</a> discharges in the later 20th century caused the rivers to become <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">heavily polluted</a>. A substantial clean-up program for both rivers is underway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-veja.abril.com.br_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-veja.abril.com.br-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www1.folha.uol.com.br_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-www1.folha.uol.com.br-29">[29]</a></sup> Neither river is navigable in the stretch that flows through the city, although <a href="/wiki/Water_transportation" title="Water transportation">water transportation</a> becomes increasingly important on the Tietê river further downstream (near <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paraná River">river Paraná</a>), as the river is part of the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Río de la Plata">River Plate</a> basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>No large natural lakes exist in the region, but the <a href="/wiki/Billings_Reservoir" title="Billings Reservoir">Billings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guarapiranga" title="Guarapiranga">Guarapiranga</a> reservoirs in the city's southern outskirts are used for <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">power generation</a>, water storage and leisure activities, such as sailing. The original <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">flora</a> consisted mainly of <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">broadleaf</a> <a href="/wiki/Evergreen" title="Evergreen">evergreens</a>. <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">Non-native species</a> are common, as the mild climate and abundant rainfall permit a multitude of tropical, subtropical and temperate plants to be cultivated, especially the ubiquitous <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The north of the municipality contains part of the 7,917 hectares (19,560 acres) <a href="/wiki/Cantareira_State_Park" title="Cantareira State Park">Cantareira State Park</a>, created in 1962, which protects a large part of the metropolitan São Paulo water supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In 2015, São Paulo experienced a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2015_Brazilian_drought" title="2015 Brazilian drought">major drought</a>, which led several cities in the state to start a rationing system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt2.2015_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt2.2015-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_biodiversity">Parks and biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Parks and biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cantareira_panorama.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Cantareira_panorama.jpg/220px-Cantareira_panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Cantareira_panorama.jpg/330px-Cantareira_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Cantareira_panorama.jpg/440px-Cantareira_panorama.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Cantareira_State_Park" title="Cantareira State Park">Cantareira State Park</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Green_belt#Brazil" title="Green belt">São Paulo Green Belt Biosphere Reserve</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parque_do_ibirapuera_visto_do_c%C3%A9u.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1080" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Parque_do_ibirapuera_visto_do_c%C3%A9u.jpg/220px-Parque_do_ibirapuera_visto_do_c%C3%A9u.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Parque_do_ibirapuera_visto_do_c%C3%A9u.jpg/330px-Parque_do_ibirapuera_visto_do_c%C3%A9u.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Parque_do_ibirapuera_visto_do_c%C3%A9u.jpg/440px-Parque_do_ibirapuera_visto_do_c%C3%A9u.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Ibirapuera_Park" title="Ibirapuera Park">Ibirapuera Park</a>, elected the best in South America by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TripAdvisor" title="TripAdvisor">TripAdvisor</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>São Paulo is located in an <a href="/wiki/Ecotone" title="Ecotone">ecotone</a> area between 3 <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biomes</a>: <a href="/wiki/Araucaria_moist_forests" title="Araucaria moist forests">mixed ombrophilous forest</a>, dense ombrophilous forest and <a href="/wiki/Cerrado" title="Cerrado">cerrado</a>; the latter had some plant species native to the <a href="/wiki/Pampas" title="Pampas">pampas</a> in the city. There were several species typical of both biomes, among them we can mention: <a href="/wiki/Araucaria" title="Araucaria">araucarias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eugenia_uniflora" title="Eugenia uniflora">pitangueiras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campomanesia_phaea" title="Campomanesia phaea">cambucís</a>, <a href="/wiki/Handroanthus" title="Handroanthus">ipês</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campomanesia_phaea" title="Campomanesia phaea">jabuticabeiras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syagrus_romanzoffiana" title="Syagrus romanzoffiana">queen palms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byrsonima_basiloba" title="Byrsonima basiloba">muricís-do-campo</a>, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Currently, little remains of the city's original vegetation and most of what is planted in the streets, squares and parks is of exotic origin and also Brazilian but from other regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Some of these species are even invasive and end up threatening and invading areas of preserved native vegetation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, São Paulo had 62 municipal and state parks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> such as the <a href="/wiki/Cantareira_State_Park" title="Cantareira State Park">Cantareira State Park</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Green_belt#Brazil" title="Green belt">São Paulo Green Belt Biosphere Reserve</a> and home to one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Urban_forest" title="Urban forest">urban forests</a> on the planet with 7,900 hectares (20,000 acres) of extension,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fontes_do_Ipiranga_State_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fontes do Ipiranga State Park (page does not exist)">Fontes do Ipiranga State Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ibirapuera_Park" title="Ibirapuera Park">Ibirapuera Park</a>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tiet%C3%AA_Ecological_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tietê Ecological Park (page does not exist)">Tietê Ecological Park</a>, the Capivari-Monos Environmental Protection Area, the <a href="/wiki/Serra_do_Mar_State_Park" title="Serra do Mar State Park">Serra do Mar State Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Villa-Lobos_State_Park" title="Villa-Lobos State Park">Villa-Lobos State Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Park_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="People's Park (São Paulo)">People's Park</a>, and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jaragu%C3%A1_State_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jaraguá State Park (page does not exist)">Jaraguá State Park</a>, listed as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> in 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, São Paulo had 2,300 hectares (5,700 acres) of green area, less than 1.5% of the city's area<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and below the 12 square metres (130 sq ft) per inhabitant recommended by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> About 21% of the municipality's area is covered by green areas, including ecological reserves (2010 data).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the municipality it is possible to observe forest birds that usually appear in the spring, due to the belt of native forest that still surrounds the metropolitan region. Species such as the <a href="/wiki/Rufous-bellied_thrush" title="Rufous-bellied thrush">rufous-bellied thrush</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden-chevroned_tanager" title="Golden-chevroned tanager">golden-chevroned tanager</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_kiskadee" title="Great kiskadee">great kiskadee</a> and hummingbird are the most common. Despite the intense pollution, the main rivers of the city, the Tietê and the Pinheiros, shelter several species of animals such as <a href="/wiki/Capybara" title="Capybara">capybaras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawk" title="Hawk">hawks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_lapwing" title="Southern lapwing">southern lapwings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heron" title="Heron">herons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nutria" title="Nutria">nutrias</a>. Other species found in the municipality are the <a href="/wiki/Gray_brocket" title="Gray brocket">gray brocket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Howler_monkey" title="Howler monkey">howler monkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green-billed_toucan" title="Green-billed toucan">green-billed toucan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Amazonian_umbrellabird" title="Amazonian umbrellabird">Amazonian umbrellabird</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_problems">Environmental problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Environmental problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:At_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_2018_331.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/At_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_2018_331.jpg/220px-At_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_2018_331.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/At_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_2018_331.jpg/330px-At_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_2018_331.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/At_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_2018_331.jpg/440px-At_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_2018_331.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_River" title="Tietê River">Tietê River</a>, one of the most polluted in the city.</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pollution_over_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(Jardins).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Pollution_over_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28Jardins%29.jpg/220px-Pollution_over_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28Jardins%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Pollution_over_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28Jardins%29.jpg/330px-Pollution_over_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28Jardins%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Pollution_over_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28Jardins%29.jpg/440px-Pollution_over_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28Jardins%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Smog" title="Smog">Smog</a> seen on the horizon of the Ibirapuera region</div></div></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">Air pollution</a> in the city is intense,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ribeiro_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ribeiro-47">[47]</a></sup> mainly due to the huge amount of cars that circulate daily on its streets, avenues and highways. The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) sets a limit of 20 micrograms of particulate matter per cubic meter of air as a safe annual average. In an assessment carried out by the WHO among over a thousand cities around the world in 2011, the city of São Paulo was ranked 268th among the most polluted, with an average rate of 38 micrograms per cubic meter, a rate well above the limit imposed by the organization, but lower than in other Brazilian cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> (64 micrograms per cubic meter).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> A 2013 study found that air pollution in the city causes more deaths than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traffic_accidents" title="Traffic accidents">traffic accidents</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pollution" title="Atmospheric pollution">atmospheric pollution</a>, the municipality has serious problems due to <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">water pollution</a>, mainly concentrated in its two main rivers, the <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_River" title="Tietê River">Tietê River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pinheiros_River" title="Pinheiros River">Pinheiros River</a>, which are highly degraded and are some of the most polluted rivers in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> However, both go through the process of depollution, with the Tietê Project having been created in 1992 and having already cost 2.7 billion dollars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-51">[51]</a></sup> In 2019, the Novo Rio Pinheiros Project was created, under the administration of <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Doria" title="João Doria">João Doria</a>, whose aim is to reduce sewage discharged into tributaries, improve water quality and revitalize the banks by 2022.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>The problem of balanced water supply for the city - and for the metropolis, in general - is also a worrying issue: São Paulo has few sources of water in its own perimeter, having to seek it in distant hydrographic basins. The problem of water pollution is also aggravated by the irregular occupation of watershed areas, caused by urban expansion, driven by the difficulty of access to land and housing in central areas by the low-income population<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> and associated with real estate speculation and precariousness in new subdivisions. With this, there is also an overvaluation of individual transport over public transport – leading to the current rate of more than one vehicle for every two inhabitants and aggravating the problem of environmental pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tempestade_em_SP.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2144" data-file-width="3216" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tempestade_em_SP.jpg/220px-Tempestade_em_SP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tempestade_em_SP.jpg/330px-Tempestade_em_SP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tempestade_em_SP.jpg/440px-Tempestade_em_SP.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tempestade_em_SP.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Heavy rain and lightning in São Paulo, which has one of the largest number of <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a> incidents amongst Brazilian state capitals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen classification</a>, the city has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<i>Cwa</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> In summer (January through March), the mean low temperature is about 19 °C (66 °F) and the mean high temperatures is near 28 °C (82 °F). In winter, temperatures tend to range between 12 and 22 °C (54 and 72 °F). The record high temperature was 37.8 °C (100.0 °F) on 17 October 2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and the lowest −3.2 °C (26.2 °F) on 25 June 1918.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Capricorn" title="Tropic of Capricorn">Tropic of Capricorn</a>, at about 23°27' S, passes through north of São Paulo and roughly marks the boundary between the tropical and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperateness" title="Temperateness">temperate</a> areas of South America. Because of its elevation, however, São Paulo experiences a more temperate climate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The city experiences four seasons. The summer is warm and rainy. Autumn and spring are transitional seasons. Winter is the coldest season, with cloudiness around town and frequently polar air masses. <a href="/wiki/Frost" title="Frost">Frosts</a> occur sporadically in regions further away from the center, in some winters throughout the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rainfall is abundant, annually averaging 1,454 millimeters (57.2 in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> It is especially common in the warmer months averaging 219 millimeters (8.6 in) and decreases in winter, averaging 47 millimeters (1.9 in). Neither São Paulo nor the nearby coast has ever been hit by a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadic</a> activity is uncommon. During late winter, especially August, the city experiences the phenomenon known as <i>"veranico"</i> or <i>"verãozinho"</i> ("little summer"), which consists of hot and dry weather, sometimes reaching temperatures well above 28 °C (82 °F). On the other hand, relatively cool days during summer are fairly common when persistent winds blow from the ocean. On such occasions daily high temperatures may not surpass 20 °C (68 °F), accompanied by lows often below 15 °C (59 °F), however, summer can be extremely hot when a heat wave hits the city followed by temperatures around 34 °C (93 °F), but in places with greater skyscraper density and less tree cover, the temperature can feel like 39 °C (102 °F), as on <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">Paulista Avenue</a> for example. In the summer of 2014, São Paulo was affected by a heat wave that lasted for almost 4 weeks with highs above 30 °C (86 °F), peaking on 36 °C (97 °F). Secondary to <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Groundwater_pollution" title="Groundwater pollution">groundwater pollution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, São Paulo is increasingly susceptible to <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">drought</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_shortage" title="Water shortage">water shortages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p>
