<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-top-width:0;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><caption style="border-top:1px #aaa solid;border-left:1px #aaa solid;border-right:1px #aaa solid;background-color:lavender;padding:0.25em;font-weight:bold">Historical population</caption><tbody><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Percent change">±%</abbr></th></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1872</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">31,385</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+106.9%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1900</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">239,820</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,198,096</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+65.7%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1960</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">3,781,446</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+72.0%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1970</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">5,924,615</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+56.7%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1980</th><td style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2000</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">10,434,252</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+8.2%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2010</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">11,253,503</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+7.9%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2021</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">12,396,372</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+10.2%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left"><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Brazilians" title="Brazilians">Brazilians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Demographics of São Paulo">Demographics of São Paulo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Brazil" title="Demographics of Brazil">Demographics of Brazil</a></div>
<p>São Paulo's population has grown rapidly. By 1960 it had surpassed that of <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, making it Brazil's most populous city. By this time, the urbanized area of São Paulo had extended beyond the boundaries of the municipality proper into neighboring municipalities, making it a metropolitan area with a population of 4.6 million. Population growth has continued since 1960, although the rate of growth has slowed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, São Paulo was the most populous city in Brazil and in South America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">2010 IBGE Census</a>, there were 11,244,369 people residing in the city of São Paulo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Portuguese remains the most widely spoken language and São Paulo is the largest city in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_speaking_world" title="Portuguese speaking world">Portuguese speaking world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, the city had 2,146,077 opposite-sex couples and 7,532 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Same-sex_couple" title="Same-sex couple">same-sex couples</a>. The population of São Paulo was 52.6% female and 47.4% male.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-censo2010.ibge.gov.br_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-censo2010.ibge.gov.br-87">[87]</a></sup> The census found 6,824,668 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Brazilian" title="White Brazilian">White</a> people (60.6%), 3,433,218 <a href="/wiki/Pardo_Brazilians" title="Pardo Brazilians">Pardo</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial#Brazil" title="Multiracial">multiracial</a>) people (30.5%), 736,083 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilian" title="Afro-Brazilian">Black</a> people (6.5%), 246,244 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Brazilian" title="Asian Brazilian">Asian</a> people (2.2%) and 21,318 <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">Amerindian</a> people (0.2%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-censo2010.ibge.gov.br_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-censo2010.ibge.gov.br-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_area">Metropolitan area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Metropolitan area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater São Paulo">Greater São Paulo</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Macrometropolis" title="São Paulo Macrometropolis">São Paulo Macrometropolis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS-67_City_lights_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brazil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3712" data-file-width="5568" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/ISS-67_City_lights_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg/220px-ISS-67_City_lights_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/ISS-67_City_lights_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg/330px-ISS-67_City_lights_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/ISS-67_City_lights_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg/440px-ISS-67_City_lights_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS-67_City_lights_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brazil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite view of <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater São Paulo">Greater São Paulo</a> at  night</div></div></div>
<p>The nonspecific term "Grande São Paulo" ("<i><a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater São Paulo">Greater São Paulo</a></i>") covers multiple definitions. The legally defined <i>Região Metropolitana de São Paulo</i> consists of 39 municipalities in total and a population of 21.1 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bra_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-bra-88">[88]</a></sup> inhabitants (as of the 2014 National Census<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>).
</p><p>The Metropolitan Region of São Paulo is known as the financial, economic, and cultural center of Brazil. Among the largest municipalities, <a href="/wiki/Guarulhos" title="Guarulhos">Guarulhos</a>, with a population of more than 1 million people is the biggest one. Several others count more than 100,000 inhabitants, such as <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Bernardo_do_Campo" title="São Bernardo do Campo">São Bernardo do Campo</a> (811,000 inh.) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santo_Andr%C3%A9" title="Santo André">Santo André</a> (707,000 inh.) in the <a href="/wiki/ABC_Region" title="ABC Region">ABC Region</a>. The ABC Region, comprising Santo André, São Bernardo do Campo and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Caetano_do_Sul" title="São Caetano do Sul">São Caetano do Sul</a> in the south of Grande São Paulo, is an important location for industrial corporations, such as <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ford_Motors" title="Ford Motors">Ford Motors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>Because São Paulo has <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a>, it uses a different definition for its metropolitan area alternately called the Expanded Metropolitan Complex of São Paulo and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Macrometropolis" title="São Paulo Macrometropolis">São Paulo Macrometropolis</a>. Analogous to the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">BosWash</a> definition, it is one of the largest urban agglomerations in the world, with 32 million inhabitants,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> behind <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">Tokyo</a>, which includes 4 contiguous legally defined metropolitan regions and 3 micro-regions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration_and_migration">Immigration and migration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Immigration and migration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">Immigration to Brazil</a></div>
<div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:287px; background: white;">

<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:yellow; width:0.2%; overflow: hidden;"> </div></td>

</tbody></table>
</div>
</div>
<p>São Paulo is considered the most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multicultural" title="Multicultural">multicultural</a> city in Brazil. From 1870 to 2010, approximately 2.3 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrants" title="Immigrants">immigrants</a> arrived in the state, from all parts of the world. The <a href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilians" title="Italian Brazilians">Italian community</a> is one of the strongest, with a presence throughout the city. Of the 9 million inhabitants of São Paulo, 50% (4.5 million people) have full or partial Italian ancestry. São Paulo has more <a href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilians" title="Italian Brazilians">descendants of Italians</a> than any Italian city (the largest city of <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> is <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, with 2.8 million inhabitants).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>The main groups, considering all the metropolitan area, are: 6 million people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilian" title="Italian Brazilian">Italian descent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> 3 million people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_Brazilian" title="Portuguese Brazilian">Portuguese descent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> 1.7 million people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_Brazilian" title="African Brazilian">African descent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> 1 million people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_Brazilian" title="Arab Brazilian">Arab descent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-95">[95]</a></sup> 665,000 people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilian" title="Japanese Brazilian">Japanese descent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-95">[95]</a></sup> 400,000 people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Brazilian" title="German Brazilian">German descent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-95">[95]</a></sup> 250,000 people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Brazilian" title="French Brazilian">French descent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_95-3"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-95">[95]</a></sup> 150,000 people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_Brazilian" title="Greek Brazilian">Greek descent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_95-4"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-95">[95]</a></sup> 120,000 people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Brazilian" title="Chinese Brazilian">Chinese descent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_95-5"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-95">[95]</a></sup> 120,000–300,000 <a href="/wiki/Bolivians_in_Brazil" title="Bolivians in Brazil">Bolivian immigrants</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> 50,000 people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_Brazilian" title="Korean Brazilian">Korean descent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> and 80,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jews_in_Brazil" title="Jews in Brazil">Jews</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>
</p><p>Even today, Italians are grouped in neighborhoods like <a href="/wiki/Bixiga" title="Bixiga">Bixiga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%A1s" title="Brás">Brás</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mooca_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Mooca (district of São Paulo)">Mooca</a> to promote celebrations and festivals. In the early twentieth century, Italian and its dialects were spoken almost as much as <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> in the city, which influenced the formation of the São Paulo dialect of today. Six thousand pizzerias are producing about a million pizzas a day. Brazil has the largest <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian population</a> outside <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, with São Paulo being the most populous city with Italian ancestry in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Brazilians" title="Portuguese Brazilians">Portuguese community</a> is also large; it is estimated that three million paulistanos have some origin in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>. The <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Brazil" title="History of the Jews in Brazil">Jewish colony</a> is more than 80,000 people in São Paulo and is concentrated mainly in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Higien%C3%B3polis,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Higienópolis, São Paulo">Higienópolis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bom_Retiro_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Bom Retiro (district of São Paulo)">Bom Retiro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbesimi_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-forbesimi-100">[100]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Italians_Sao_Paulo_-_original.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1428" data-file-width="2009" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Italians_Sao_Paulo_-_original.jpg/220px-Italians_Sao_Paulo_-_original.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Italians_Sao_Paulo_-_original.jpg/330px-Italians_Sao_Paulo_-_original.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Italians_Sao_Paulo_-_original.jpg/440px-Italians_Sao_Paulo_-_original.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Italians_Sao_Paulo_-_original.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilian" title="Italian Brazilian">Italian immigrants</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Immigrant_Inn" title="Immigrant Inn">Immigrant Inn</a>, c. 1890</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Liberdade_of_Sao_Paulo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4825" data-file-width="5641" decoding="async" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Liberdade_of_Sao_Paulo.jpg/220px-Liberdade_of_Sao_Paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Liberdade_of_Sao_Paulo.jpg/330px-Liberdade_of_Sao_Paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Liberdade_of_Sao_Paulo.jpg/440px-Liberdade_of_Sao_Paulo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Liberdade_of_Sao_Paulo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Liberdade_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Liberdade (district of São Paulo)">Liberdade</a> district is a <a href="/wiki/Japantown" title="Japantown">Japantown</a> of São Paulo</div></div></div>
<p>From the nineteenth century through the first half of the twentieth century, São Paulo also received <a href="/wiki/German_Brazilians" title="German Brazilians">German immigrants</a> (in the current neighborhood of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santo_Amaro,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Santo Amaro, São Paulo">Santo Amaro</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithuanian_people" title="Lithuanian people">Lithuanian</a> (in the neighborhood <a href="/wiki/Vila_Zelina" title="Vila Zelina">Vila Zelina</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbesimi_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-forbesimi-100">[100]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"A French observer, travelling to São Paulo at the time, noted that there was a division of the capitalist class, by nationality (...) Germans, French and Italians shared the dry goods sector with Brazilians. Foodstuffs was generally the province of either Portuguese or Brazilians, except for bakery and pastry which was the domain of the French and Germans. Shoes and tinware were mostly controlled by Italians. However, the larger metallurgical plants were in the hands of the English and the Americans. (...) Italians outnumbered Brazilians two to one in São Paulo."</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<p>Until 1920, 1,078,437 <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italians</a> entered in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="State of São Paulo">State of São Paulo</a>. Of the immigrants who arrived there between 1887 and 1902, 63.5% came from Italy. Between 1888 and 1919, 44.7% of the immigrants were Italians, 19.2% were <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spaniards</a> and 15.4% were <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100_anos_de_imigração_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-100_anos_de_imigração-102">[102]</a></sup> In 1920, nearly 80% of São Paulo city's population was composed of immigrants and their descendants and Italians made up over half of its male population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100_anos_de_imigração_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-100_anos_de_imigração-102">[102]</a></sup> At that time, the Governor of São Paulo said that <i>"if the owner of each house in São Paulo display the flag of the country of origin on the roof, from above São Paulo would look like an Italian city".</i> In 1900, a columnist who was absent from São Paulo for 20 years wrote <i>"then São Paulo used to be a genuine Paulista city, today it is an Italian city."</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100_anos_de_imigração_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-100_anos_de_imigração-102">[102]</a></sup>
</p><p>São Paulo also is home of the largest <a href="/wiki/Japanese_diaspora" title="Japanese diaspora">Japanese community</a> outside <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> In 1958 the census counted 120,000 Japanese in the city and by 1987, there were 326,000 with another 170,000 in the surrounding areas within São Paulo state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lesserp3_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lesserp3-104">[104]</a></sup> As of 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_community_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Japanese community of São Paulo">Paulistano Japanese population</a> outnumbered their fellow diaspora in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Peruvian" title="Japanese Peruvian">the entirety of Peru</a>, and in all individual American cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lesserp3_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lesserp3-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>Research conducted by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="University of São Paulo">University of São Paulo</a> (USP) shows the city's high ethnic diversity: when asked if they are "descendants of foreign immigrants", 81% of the students reported "yes". The main reported ancestries were: Italian (30.5%), Portuguese (23%), Spanish (14%), Japanese (8%), German (6%), <i>Brazilian</i> (4%), African (3%), Arab (2%) and Jewish (1%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>
</p><p>The city once attracted numerous immigrants from all over Brazil and even from foreign countries, due to a strong economy and for being the hub of most Brazilian companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> São Paulo is also receiving waves of immigration from <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> and from many countries of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>. Those immigrants are mainly concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Pra%C3%A7a_da_S%C3%A9" title="Praça da Sé">Praça da Sé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glic%C3%A9rio" title="Glicério">Glicério</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vale_do_Anhangaba%C3%BA" title="Vale do Anhangabaú">Vale do Anhangabaú</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Zone_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Central Zone of São Paulo">Central Zone of São Paulo</a>.
</p><p>Since the 19th century people began migrating from <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Region,_Brazil" title="Northeast Region, Brazil">northeastern Brazil</a> into São Paulo. This migration grew enormously in the 1930s and remained huge in the next decades. The concentration of land, modernization in rural areas, changes in work relationships and cycles of droughts stimulated migration. Northeastern migrants live mainly in hazardous and unhealthy areas of the city, in <a href="/wiki/Corti%C3%A7o" title="Cortiço">cortiços</a> <i>("guettos")</i>, in <a href="/wiki/Favela" title="Favela">favelas</a> <i>("slums")</i> of the metropolis, because they offer cheaper housing. The largest concentration of northeastern migrants was found in the area of Sé/Brás (districts of <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%A1s" title="Brás">Brás</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bom_Retiro,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Bom Retiro, São Paulo">Bom Retiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambuci_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Cambuci (district of São Paulo)">Cambuci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pari_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Pari (district of São Paulo)">Pari</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Sé (district of São Paulo)">Sé</a>). In this area they composed 41% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Brazil" title="Religion in Brazil">Religion in Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Brazil" title="Protestantism in Brazil">Protestantism in Brazil</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church_in_Brazil" title="Roman Catholic Church in Brazil">Roman Catholic Church in Brazil</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:298px;max-width:298px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Webysther_20190306142509_-_Catedral_Metropolitana_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2992" data-file-width="1870" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Webysther_20190306142509_-_Catedral_Metropolitana_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/150px-Webysther_20190306142509_-_Catedral_Metropolitana_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Webysther_20190306142509_-_Catedral_Metropolitana_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/225px-Webysther_20190306142509_-_Catedral_Metropolitana_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Webysther_20190306142509_-_Catedral_Metropolitana_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/300px-Webysther_20190306142509_-_Catedral_Metropolitana_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Cathedral" title="São Paulo Cathedral">São Paulo Cathedral</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Downtown São Paulo">Downtown São Paulo</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:142px;max-width:142px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monasterio_de_Sao_Bento.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="9769" data-file-width="5748" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Monasterio_de_Sao_Bento.jpg/140px-Monasterio_de_Sao_Bento.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Monasterio_de_Sao_Bento.jpg/210px-Monasterio_de_Sao_Bento.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Monasterio_de_Sao_Bento.jpg/280px-Monasterio_de_Sao_Bento.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Mosteiro_de_S%C3%A3o_Bento_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Mosteiro de São Bento (São Paulo)">São Bento Monastery</a>.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Like the cultural variety verifiable in São Paulo, there are several religious manifestations present in the city. Although it has developed on an eminently <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> social matrix, both due to colonization and immigration – and even today most of the people of São Paulo declare themselves Roman Catholic – it is possible to find in the city dozens of different Protestant denominations, as well as the practice of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spiritism" title="Spiritism">Spiritism</a>, among others. <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> and Eastern religions also have relevance among the beliefs most practiced by Paulistanos. It is estimated that there are more than one hundred thousand <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> followers and Hindu. Also considerable are <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormonism</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilian_religions" title="Afro-Brazilian religions">Afro-Brazilian religions</a>.
</p><p>According to data from the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics</a> (IBGE), in 2010 the population of São Paulo was 6,549,775 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> (58.2%), 2,887,810 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">Protestants</a> (22.1%), 531,822 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spiritists" title="Spiritists">Spiritists</a> (4.7 percent), 101,493 <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (0.9 percent), 75,075 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhists" title="Buddhists">Buddhists</a> (0.7 percent), 50,794 <a href="/wiki/Umbanda" title="Umbanda">Umbandists</a> (0.5 percent), 43,610 <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> (0.4 percent), 28,673 <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Catholic_Apostolic_Church" title="Brazilian Catholic Apostolic Church">Catholic Apostolic Brazilians</a> (0.3%), 25,583 eastern religious (0.2%), 18,058 <a href="/wiki/Candombl%C3%A9" title="Candomblé">Candomblecists</a> (0.2%), 17,321 <a href="/wiki/Mormons" title="Mormons">Mormons</a> (0.2%), 14,894 Eastern Orthodox (0.1%), 9,119 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spiritualists" title="Spiritualists">spiritualists</a> (0.1%), 8,277 <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> (0.1%), 7,139 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esoteric" title="Esoteric">esoteric</a> (0.1%), 1,829 practiced Indian traditions (&lt;0.1%) and 1,008 were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> (&lt;0.1%). Others 1,056 008 had no religion (9.4%), 149,628 followed other Christian religiosities (1.3%), 55,978 had an undetermined religion or multiple belonging (0.5%), 14,127 did not know (0.1%) And 1,896 reported following other religiosities (&lt;0.1%).
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:423px;max-width:423px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:217px;max-width:217px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Temple-salomon-de-sao-paulo.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="434" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Temple-salomon-de-sao-paulo.jpg/215px-Temple-salomon-de-sao-paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Temple-salomon-de-sao-paulo.jpg/323px-Temple-salomon-de-sao-paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Temple-salomon-de-sao-paulo.jpg/430px-Temple-salomon-de-sao-paulo.jpg 2x" width="215"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Solomon_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Temple of Solomon (São Paulo)">Temple of Solomon</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Church_of_the_Kingdom_of_God" title="Universal Church of the Kingdom of God">Universal Church of the Kingdom of God</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catedral_Metropolitana_Ortodoxa_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1773" data-file-width="2288" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Catedral_Metropolitana_Ortodoxa_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28cropped%29.jpg/200px-Catedral_Metropolitana_Ortodoxa_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Catedral_Metropolitana_Ortodoxa_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Catedral_Metropolitana_Ortodoxa_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Catedral_Metropolitana_Ortodoxa_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28cropped%29.jpg/400px-Catedral_Metropolitana_Ortodoxa_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Catedral_Metropolitana_Ortodoxa" title="Catedral Metropolitana Ortodoxa">Metropolitan Orthodox Cathedral</a> of São Paulo</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The Catholic Church divides the territory of the municipality of São Paulo into four ecclesiastical circumscriptions: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Archdiocese of São Paulo">Archdiocese of São Paulo</a>, and the adjacent Diocese of Santo Amaro, the Diocese of São Miguel Paulista and the Diocese of Campo Limpo, the last three suffragans of the first. The archive of the archdiocese, called the Metropolitan Archival Dom Duarte Leopoldo e Silva, in the <a href="/wiki/Ipiranga_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Ipiranga (district of São Paulo)">Ipiranga</a> neighborhood, holds one of the most important documentary heritage in Brazil. The archiepiscopal is the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Cathedral" title="São Paulo Cathedral">Metropolitan Cathedral of São Paulo</a> (known as Sé Cathedral), in <a href="/wiki/Pra%C3%A7a_da_S%C3%A9" title="Praça da Sé">Praça da Sé</a>, considered one of the five largest <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic</a> temples in the world. The Catholic Church recognizes as patron saints of the city <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">Saint Paul of Tarsus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Pe%C3%B1afrancia" title="Our Lady of Peñafrancia">Our Lady of Penha of France</a>.
</p><p>The city has the most diverse Protestant or Reformed creeds, such as the Evangelical Community of Our Land, Maranatha Christian Church, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran_Church" title="Lutheran Church">Lutheran Church</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church" title="Presbyterian Church">Presbyterian Church</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methodist_Church" title="Methodist Church">Methodist Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Episcopal_Church" title="Anglican Episcopal Church">Anglican Episcopal Church</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist_church" title="Baptist church">Baptist churches</a>, Assembly Church of God, The <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>, the World Church of God's Power, the Universal Church of the Kingdom of God, the Christian Congregation in Brazil, among others, as well as Christians of various denominations.
</p><p><i>Source: <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">IBGE</a> 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </i>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_security">Public security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Public security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Formacaodapmesp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1312" data-file-width="1968" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Formacaodapmesp.jpg/220px-Formacaodapmesp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Formacaodapmesp.jpg/330px-Formacaodapmesp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Formacaodapmesp.jpg/440px-Formacaodapmesp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Formacaodapmesp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Training of soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/Military_Police_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_State" title="Military Police of São Paulo State">Military Police of São Paulo State</a> at the Military Police Academy of Barro Branco</div></div></div>
<p>According to the 2011 Global Homicide Survey released by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, in the period between 2004 and 2009 the homicide rate dropped from 20.8 to 10.8 murders per 100,000 inhabitants. The UN pointed to São Paulo as an example of how big cities can reduce crime. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crime_rates" title="Crime rates">Crime rates</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Homicide" title="Homicide">homicide</a>, have been steadily declining for 8 years. The number of murders in 2007 was 63% lower than in 1999. Carandiru's 9th DP is considered one of the five best police stations in the world and the best in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.
</p><p>In 2008, the city of São Paulo ranked 493rd in the list of the most violent cities in Brazil. Among the capitals, it was the fourth least violent, registering, in 2006, homicide rates higher than those of <a href="/wiki/Boa_Vista,_Roraima" title="Boa Vista, Roraima">Boa Vista</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palmas,_Tocantins" title="Palmas, Tocantins">Palmas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natal,_Rio_Grande_do_Norte" title="Natal, Rio Grande do Norte">Natal</a>.
</p><p>In a survey on the Adolescent Homicide Index (IHA), released in 2009, São Paulo ranked 151st among 267 cities with more than 100,000 inhabitants. In November 2009, the Ministry of Justice and the Brazilian Forum of Public Security published a survey that pointed to São Paulo as the safest Brazilian capital for young people. Between 2000 and 2010, the city of São Paulo reduced its homicide rate by 78%. According to data from the Map of Violence 2011, published by the Sangari Institute and the Ministry of Justice, the city of São Paulo has the lowest homicide rate per 100,000 inhabitants among all Brazilian capitals.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_challenges">Social challenges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Social challenges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parais%C3%B3polis_I.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2666" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Parais%C3%B3polis_I.jpg/220px-Parais%C3%B3polis_I.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Parais%C3%B3polis_I.jpg/330px-Parais%C3%B3polis_I.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Parais%C3%B3polis_I.jpg/440px-Parais%C3%B3polis_I.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parais%C3%B3polis_I.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parais%C3%B3polis_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Paraisópolis (São Paulo)">Paraisópolis</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">slum</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Favela" title="Favela">favela</a></i>) in the city, with residential buildings in the background</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Conjunto_habitacional_em_Heli%C3%B3polis.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2750" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Conjunto_habitacional_em_Heli%C3%B3polis.jpg/220px-Conjunto_habitacional_em_Heli%C3%B3polis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Conjunto_habitacional_em_Heli%C3%B3polis.jpg/330px-Conjunto_habitacional_em_Heli%C3%B3polis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Conjunto_habitacional_em_Heli%C3%B3polis.jpg/440px-Conjunto_habitacional_em_Heli%C3%B3polis.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Conjunto_habitacional_em_Heli%C3%B3polis.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Public_housing" title="Public housing">Public housing</a> in <a href="/wiki/Heli%C3%B3polis" title="Heliópolis">Heliópolis</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Social_issues_in_Brazil" title="Social issues in Brazil">Social issues in Brazil</a></div>
<p>Since the beginning of the 20th century, São Paulo has been a major economic center in Latin America. During two <a href="/wiki/World_war" title="World war">World Wars</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, coffee exports (from other regions of the state) were critically affected. This led wealthy coffee farmers to invest in industrial activities that turned São Paulo into Brazil's largest industrial hub.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Crime_statistics" title="Crime statistics">Crime rates</a> consistently decreased in the 21st century. The citywide homicide rate was 6.56 in 2019, less than a fourth of the 27.38 national rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li>Air quality<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ribeiro_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ribeiro-47">[47]</a></sup> has steadily increased during the modern era.</li>
<li>The two major rivers crossing the city, <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_River" title="Tietê River">Tietê</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pinheiros_River" title="Pinheiros River">Pinheiros</a>, are highly polluted. A major project to clean up these rivers is underway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-veja.abril.com.br_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-veja.abril.com.br-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www1.folha.uol.com.br_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-www1.folha.uol.com.br-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Cidade_Limpa" title="Cidade Limpa">Clean City Law</a> or anti<a href="/wiki/Billboard" title="Billboard">billboard</a>, approved in 2007, focused on two main targets: anti-publicity and anti-commerce. Advertisers estimate that they removed 15,000 billboards and that more than 1,600 <a href="/wiki/Signage" title="Signage">signs</a> and 1,300 towering metal panels were dismantled by authorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li>São Paulo metropolitan region, adopted vehicle restrictions from 1996 to 1998 to reduce air pollution during wintertime. Since 1997, a similar project was implemented throughout the year in the central area of São Paulo to improve traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></li>
<li>There were more than 30,000 homeless people in 2021 according to official data. It increased by 31% in two years, and doubled in 20 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Brazil" title="Languages of Brazil">Languages of Brazil</a></div>
<p>The primary language is <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>. The general language from São Paulo General, or <a href="/wiki/Tupi_language" title="Tupi language">Tupi Austral</a> (Southern Tupi), was the Tupi-based trade language of what is now São Vicente, São Paulo, and the upper Tietê River. In the 17th century it was widely spoken in São Paulo and spread to neighboring regions while in Brazil. From 1750 on, following orders from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marquess_of_Pombal" title="Marquess of Pombal">Marquess of Pombal</a>, Portuguese language was introduced through immigration and consequently taught to children in schools. The original <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tupi_Austral" title="Tupi Austral">Tupi Austral</a> language subsequently lost ground to <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, and eventually became extinct. Due to the large influx of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilians" title="Japanese Brazilians">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Brazilians" title="German Brazilians">German</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilians_of_Spanish_descent" title="Brazilians of Spanish descent">Spanish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Brazilian" title="Italian Brazilian">Italian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_Brazilian" title="Arab Brazilian">Arab</a> immigrants etc., the Portuguese idiom spoken in the metropolitan area of São Paulo reflects influences from those languages.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Interior_do_Museu_da_L%C3%ADngua_Portuguesa_em_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brasil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3504" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Interior_do_Museu_da_L%C3%ADngua_Portuguesa_em_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg/220px-Interior_do_Museu_da_L%C3%ADngua_Portuguesa_em_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Interior_do_Museu_da_L%C3%ADngua_Portuguesa_em_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg/330px-Interior_do_Museu_da_L%C3%ADngua_Portuguesa_em_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Interior_do_Museu_da_L%C3%ADngua_Portuguesa_em_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg/440px-Interior_do_Museu_da_L%C3%ADngua_Portuguesa_em_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Interior_do_Museu_da_L%C3%ADngua_Portuguesa_em_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brasil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Museum of the Portuguese Language">Museum of the Portuguese Language</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Italian influence in São Paulo accents is evident in the Italian neighborhoods such as Bela Vista, <a href="/wiki/Mooca_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Mooca (district of São Paulo)">Mooca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%A1s" title="Brás">Brás</a> and Lapa. Italian mingled with Portuguese and as an old influence, was assimilated or disappeared into spoken language. The local accent with Italian influences became notorious through the songs of <a href="/wiki/Adoniran_Barbosa" title="Adoniran Barbosa">Adoniran Barbosa</a>, a Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Samba" title="Samba">samba</a> singer born to Italian parents who used to sing using the local accent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other languages spoken in the city are mainly among the Asian community: São Paulo is home to the largest Japanese population outside Japan. Although today most Japanese-Brazilians speak only Portuguese, some of them are still fluent in Japanese. Some people of Chinese and Korean descent are still able to speak their ancestral languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> In some areas it is still possible to find descendants of immigrants who speak German<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> (especially in the area of Brooklin paulista) and Russian or East European languages (especially in the area of Vila Zelina).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> In the west zone of São Paulo, specially at Vila Anastácio and Lapa region, there is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" title="Hungarian people">Hungarian</a> colony, with three churches (Calvinist, Baptist and Catholic), so on Sundays it is possible to see Hungarians talking to each other on sidewalks.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_diversity">Sexual diversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sexual diversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Brazil" title="LGBT rights in Brazil">LGBT rights in Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_people_in_Brazil" title="LGBT people in Brazil">LGBT people in Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_history_in_Brazil" title="LGBT history in Brazil">LGBT history in Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Brazil" title="Same-sex marriage in Brazil">Same-sex marriage in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A3o_Paulo_LGBT_Pride_Parade_2014_(14108541924).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_LGBT_Pride_Parade_2014_%2814108541924%29.jpg/220px-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_LGBT_Pride_Parade_2014_%2814108541924%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_LGBT_Pride_Parade_2014_%2814108541924%29.jpg/330px-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_LGBT_Pride_Parade_2014_%2814108541924%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_LGBT_Pride_Parade_2014_%2814108541924%29.jpg/440px-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_LGBT_Pride_Parade_2014_%2814108541924%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A3o_Paulo_LGBT_Pride_Parade_2014_(14108541924).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 18th edition of the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Gay_Pride_Parade" title="São Paulo Gay Pride Parade">São Paulo Gay Pride Parade</a> in 2014</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater São Paulo">Greater São Paulo</a> is home to a prominent self-identifying <a href="/wiki/Gay" title="Gay">gay</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bisexual" title="Bisexual">bisexual</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> community, with 9.6% of the male population and 7% of the female population declaring themselves to be non-heterosexual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Same-sex <a href="/wiki/Civil_union" title="Civil union">civil unions</a> have been legal in the whole country since 5 May 2011, while <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Brazil" title="Same-sex marriage in Brazil">same-sex marriage in São Paulo</a> was legalized on 18 December 2012. Since 1997, the city has hosted the annual <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Gay_Pride_Parade" title="São Paulo Gay Pride Parade">São Paulo Gay Pride Parade</a>, considered the biggest <a href="/wiki/Pride_parade" title="Pride parade">pride parade</a> in the world by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_World_Records" title="Guinness Book of World Records">Guinness Book of World Records</a> with over 5 million participants, and typically rivalling the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_City_Pride_March" title="New York City Pride March">New York City Pride March</a> for the record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCWorld'sLargestPrideParade_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYCWorld'sLargestPrideParade-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>Strongly supported by the State and the City of São Paulo government authorities, in 2010, the city hall of São Paulo invested R$1 million reais in the parade and provided a solid security plan, with approximately 2,000 policemen, two mobile police stations for immediate reporting of occurrences, 30 equipped ambulances, 55 nurses, 46 medical physicians, three hospital camps with 80 beds. The parade, considered the city's second largest event after the <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a>, begins at the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Museum_of_Art" title="São Paulo Museum of Art">São Paulo Museum of Art</a>, crosses <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">Paulista Avenue</a>, and follows Consolação Street to <a href="/wiki/Pra%C3%A7a_Roosevelt" title="Praça Roosevelt">Praça Roosevelt</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Downtown São Paulo">Downtown São Paulo</a>. According to the LGBT app <a href="/wiki/Grindr" title="Grindr">Grindr</a>, the gay parade of the city was elected the best in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:University_sao_paulo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/University_sao_paulo.jpg/220px-University_sao_paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/University_sao_paulo.jpg/330px-University_sao_paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/University_sao_paulo.jpg/440px-University_sao_paulo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:University_sao_paulo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/University_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="University of São Paulo">University of São Paulo</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Brazil" title="Education in Brazil">Education in Brazil</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_science_and_technology" title="Brazilian science and technology">Brazilian science and technology</a></div>
<p>São Paulo has public and private primary and secondary schools and vocational-<a href="/wiki/Technical_school" title="Technical school">technical schools</a>. More than nine-tenths of the population are literate and roughly the same proportion of those age 7 to 14 are enrolled in school. There are 578 universities in the state of São Paulo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p><p>The city of São Paulo is also home to research and development facilities and attracts companies due to the presence of regionally renowned universities. Science, technology and innovation is leveraged by the allocation of funds from the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">state government</a>, mainly carried out by means of the Foundation to Research Support in the State of São Paulo (Fundação de Amparo à Pesquisa do Estado de São Paulo – FAPESP), one of the main agencies promoting scientific and technological research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Health care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Brazil" title="Health in Brazil">Health in Brazil</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rede_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Saud%C3%A1vel" title="Rede São Paulo Saudável">Rede São Paulo Saudável</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Instituto_do_C%C3%A2ncer_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Octavio_Frias_de_Oliveira.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5099" data-file-width="3322" decoding="async" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Instituto_do_C%C3%A2ncer_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Octavio_Frias_de_Oliveira.jpg/170px-Instituto_do_C%C3%A2ncer_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Octavio_Frias_de_Oliveira.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Instituto_do_C%C3%A2ncer_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Octavio_Frias_de_Oliveira.jpg/255px-Instituto_do_C%C3%A2ncer_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Octavio_Frias_de_Oliveira.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Instituto_do_C%C3%A2ncer_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Octavio_Frias_de_Oliveira.jpg/340px-Instituto_do_C%C3%A2ncer_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Octavio_Frias_de_Oliveira.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Instituto_do_C%C3%A2ncer_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Octavio_Frias_de_Oliveira.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Cancer_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Institute of Cancer of São Paulo">Institute of Cancer of São Paulo</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/Oncology" title="Oncology">oncology</a> center in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>São Paulo is one of the largest health care hubs in Latin America. Among its hospitals are the Albert Einstein Israelites Hospital, ranked the best hospital in all Latin America<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Hospital_das_Cl%C3%ADnicas_da_Universidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Hospital das Clínicas da Universidade de São Paulo">Hospital das Clínicas</a>, the largest in the region, with a total area of 600,000 square meters and offers 2,400 beds, distributed among its eight specialized institutes and two assisting hospitals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup>
</p><p>The main hospitals in the city of São Paulo concentrate in the upper-income areas, the majority of the population of the city has a private health insurance. This can includes hospitals, private practices and pharmacies. The city of São Paulo has the largest number of foreigners comparing with any other Brazilian city and an intense <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_tourism" title="Health tourism">health tourism</a>. In Brazil, the city of São Paulo has the largest number of doctors who can speak more than one language, which in this case is <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, with the secondary languages predominantly are <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p><p>The private health care sector is very large and most of Brazil's best hospitals are in the city. As of September 2009, the city of São Paulo had: 32,553 <a href="/wiki/Ambulatory" title="Ambulatory">ambulatory</a> clinics, centers and professional offices (physicians, dentists and others); 217 hospitals, with 32,554 beds; 137,745 health care professionals, including 28,316 physicians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>The municipal government operates public <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_facilities" title="Health facilities">health facilities</a> across the city's territory, with 770 primary health care units (UBS), ambulatory and emergency clinics and 17 hospitals. The Municipal Secretary of Health has 59,000 employees, including 8,000 physicians and 12,000 nurses. 6,000,000 citizens uses the facilities, which provide drugs at no cost and manage an extensive family health program (PSF – Programa de Saúde da Família).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIGA_Saúde_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-SIGA_Saúde-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Sistema Integrado de Gestão de Assistência à Saúde de São Paulo – SIGA Saúde (<i>Integrated Health Care Management System in São Paulo</i>) has been operating in the city of São Paulo since 2004. Today there are more than 22 million registered users, including the people of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater São Paulo">Greater São Paulo</a>, with a monthly average of 1.3 million appointments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIGA_Saúde_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-SIGA_Saúde-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="List of mayors of São Paulo">List of mayors of São Paulo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matarazzo_Building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1680" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Matarazzo_Building.jpg/220px-Matarazzo_Building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Matarazzo_Building.jpg/330px-Matarazzo_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Matarazzo_Building.jpg/440px-Matarazzo_Building.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matarazzo_Building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Matarazzo_Building" title="Matarazzo Building">Matarazzo Building</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seat_of_local_government" title="Seat of local government">São Paulo city hall</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_Anchieta_(SP).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="748" data-file-width="965" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Pal%C3%A1cio_Anchieta_%28SP%29.jpg/220px-Pal%C3%A1cio_Anchieta_%28SP%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Pal%C3%A1cio_Anchieta_%28SP%29.jpg/330px-Pal%C3%A1cio_Anchieta_%28SP%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Pal%C3%A1cio_Anchieta_%28SP%29.jpg/440px-Pal%C3%A1cio_Anchieta_%28SP%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_Anchieta_(SP).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Municipal_Chamber_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Municipal Chamber of São Paulo">Municipal Chamber of São Paulo</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Bandeirantes_foto001_(43944820834).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3333" data-file-width="5000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Bandeirantes_foto001_%2843944820834%29.jpg/220px-Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Bandeirantes_foto001_%2843944820834%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Bandeirantes_foto001_%2843944820834%29.jpg/330px-Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Bandeirantes_foto001_%2843944820834%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Bandeirantes_foto001_%2843944820834%29.jpg/440px-Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Bandeirantes_foto001_%2843944820834%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Bandeirantes_foto001_(43944820834).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Bandeirantes" title="Palácio dos Bandeirantes">Bandeirantes Palace</a>, the seat of state government</div></div></div>
<p>As the capital of the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">state of São Paulo</a>, the city is home to the <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_dos_Bandeirantes" title="Palácio dos Bandeirantes">Bandeirantes Palace</a> (state government) and the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Legislative Assembly of São Paulo">Legislative Assembly</a>. The Executive Branch of the municipality of São Paulo is represented by the <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a> and his cabinet of secretaries, following the model proposed by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Brazil" title="Constitution of Brazil">Federal Constitution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The organic law of the municipality and the Master Plan of the city, however, determine that the public administration must guarantee to the population effective tools of manifestation of participatory democracy, which causes that the city is divided in regional prefectures, each one led by a Regional Mayor appointed by the Mayor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-districts_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-districts-129">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>The legislative power is represented by the Municipal Chamber, composed of 55 aldermen elected to four-year posts (in compliance with the provisions of Article 29 of the Constitution, which dictates a minimum number of 42 and a maximum of 55 for municipalities with more than five million inhabitants). It is up to the house to draft and vote fundamental laws for the administration and the Executive, especially the municipal budget (known as the Law of Budgetary Guidelines).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> In addition to the legislative process and the work of the secretariats, there are also a number of municipal councils, each dealing with different topics, composed of representatives of the various sectors of organized civil society. The actual performance and representativeness of such councils, however, are sometimes questioned.
</p><p>The following municipal councils are active: Municipal Council for Children and Adolescents (CMDCA); of Informatics (WCC); of the Physically Disabled (CMDP); of Education (CME); of Housing (CMH); of Environment (CADES); of Health (CMS); of Tourism (COMTUR); of Human Rights (CMDH); of Culture (CMC); and of Social Assistance (COMAS) and Drugs and Alcohol (COMUDA). The Prefecture also owns (or is the majority partner in their social capital) a series of companies responsible for various aspects of public services and the economy of São Paulo:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Anhembi_Convention_Center" title="Anhembi Convention Center"><i>São Paulo Turismo S/A</i></a> (SPTuris): company responsible for organizing large events and promoting the city's tourism.</li>
<li><i>Companhia de Engenharia de Tráfego</i> (CET):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> subordinated to the Municipal Transportation Department, is responsible for traffic supervision, fines (in cooperation with DETRAN) and maintenance of the city's road system.</li>
<li><i>Companhia Metropolitana de Habitação de São Paulo</i> (COHAB): subordinate to the Department of Housing, is responsible for the implementation of public housing policies, especially the construction of housing developments.</li>
<li><i>Empresa Municipal de Urbanização de São Paulo</i> (EMURB): subordinate to the Planning Department, is responsible for urban works and for the maintenance of public spaces and urban furniture.</li>
<li><i>Companhia de Processamento de Dados de São Paulo</i> (PRODAM): responsible for the electronic infrastructure and information technology of the city hall.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SPTrans" title="SPTrans"><i>São Paulo Transportes Sociedade Anônima</i></a> (SPTrans): responsible for the operation of the public transport systems managed by the city hall, such as the municipal bus lines.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>São Paulo is divided into 32 <a href="/wiki/Subprefecture" title="Subprefecture">subprefectures</a>, each with an administration ("subprefeitura") divided into several districts ("distritos").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-districts_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-districts-129">[129]</a></sup> The city also has a radial division into nine zones for purpose of traffic control and bus lines, which don't fit into the administrative divisions. These zones are identified by colors in the street signs. The historical core of São Paulo, which includes the inner city and the area of <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">Paulista Avenue</a>, is in the <a href="/wiki/Subprefecture_of_S%C3%A9" title="Subprefecture of Sé">Subprefecture of Sé</a>. Most other economic and tourist facilities of the city are inside an area officially called <i>Centro Expandido</i> (Portuguese for "Broad Center", or "Broad Downtown"), which includes Sé and several other subprefectures, and areas immediately around it.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Brazil" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Brazil">List of twin towns and sister cities in Brazil</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Economy of São Paulo">Economy of São Paulo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil" title="Economy of Brazil">Economy of Brazil</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Avenida_Paulista_no_p%C3%B4r_do_sol.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3990" data-file-width="5984" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Avenida_Paulista_no_p%C3%B4r_do_sol.jpg/220px-Avenida_Paulista_no_p%C3%B4r_do_sol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Avenida_Paulista_no_p%C3%B4r_do_sol.jpg/330px-Avenida_Paulista_no_p%C3%B4r_do_sol.jpg 1.5x, href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">Paulista Avenue</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a
