srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg/330px-Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg/440px-Rua_Oscar_Freire.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Rua_Oscar_Freire" title="Rua Oscar Freire">Oscar Freire St.</a>, one of the most luxurious streets in the world<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1918" data-file-width="3612" decoding="async" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/220px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/330px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg/440px-Sao_Paulo_Stock_Exchange.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/B3_(stock_exchange)" title="B3 (stock exchange)">São Paulo Stock Exchange</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Contrastes_cotidiano_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="888" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Contrastes_cotidiano_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Contrastes_cotidiano_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Contrastes_cotidiano_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Contrastes_cotidiano_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Contrastes_cotidiano_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Contrastes_cotidiano_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Park_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="People's Park (São Paulo)">People's Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Itaim_Bibi" title="Itaim Bibi">Itaim Bibi</a>, a district in the <a href="/wiki/Subprefecture_of_Pinheiros" title="Subprefecture of Pinheiros">subprefecture of Pinheiros</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>São Paulo is considered the "financial capital of Brazil", as it is the location for the headquarters of major corporations and of banks and financial institutions. São Paulo is <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil" title="Economy of Brazil">Brazil's highest GDP city</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">10th largest in the world</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Estadão_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Estadão-135">[135]</a></sup> using <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">Purchasing power parity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to data from the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Institute_of_Geography_and_Statistics" title="Brazilian Institute of Geography and Statistics">IBGE</a>, its gross domestic product (GDP) in 2010 was R$450 billion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> approximately
<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$220</span> billion, 12.26% of Brazilian GDP and 36% of all production of <a href="/wiki/Goods_and_services" title="Goods and services">goods and services</a> of the State of São Paulo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a> average annual economic growth of the city is 4.2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> São Paulo also has a large "informal" economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> In 2005, the city of São Paulo collected R$90 billion in taxes and the city budget was R$15 billion. The city has 1,500 bank <a href="/wiki/Branch" title="Branch">branches</a> and 70 shopping malls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, São Paulo is the third largest exporting municipality in Brazil after <a href="/wiki/Parauapebas" title="Parauapebas">Parauapebas, PA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro, RJ</a>. In that year São Paulo's exported goods totaled $7.32B (USD) or 3.02% of Brazil's total exports. The top five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commodities" title="Commodities">commodities</a> exported by São Paulo are <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybean</a> (21%), <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">raw sugar</a> (19%), <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> (6.5%), <a href="/wiki/Pulp_(paper)" title="Pulp (paper)">sulfate chemical wood pulp</a> (5.6%), and <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a> (4.4%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BM%26F_Bovespa" title="BM&amp;F Bovespa">São Paulo Stock Exchange</a> (BM&amp;F Bovespa) is Brazil's official stock and bond exchange. It is the largest <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> in Latin America, trading about R$6 billion (US$3.5 billion) every day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>São Paulo's economy is going through a deep transformation. Once a city with a strong <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">industrial character</a>, São Paulo's economy has followed the global trend of shifting to the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">tertiary sector of the economy</a>, focusing on services. The city is unique among Brazilian cities for its large number of foreign corporations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>63% of all the <a href="/wiki/Company" title="Company">international companies</a> with business in Brazil have their head offices in São Paulo. São Paulo has one of the largest concentrations of German businesses worldwide<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> and is the largest Swedish industrial hub alongside Gothenburg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup>
</p><p>São Paulo ranked second after New York in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FDi_magazine" title="FDi magazine">FDi magazine</a>'s bi-annual ranking of Cities of the Future 2013–14 in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, and was named the Latin American City of the Future 2013–14, overtaking <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Chile" title="Santiago de Chile">Santiago de Chile</a>, the first city in the previous ranking. Santiago now ranks second, followed by <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>
</p><p>The per capita income for the city was R$32,493 in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Mercer_(consulting_firm)" title="Mercer (consulting firm)">Mercer</a>'s 2011 <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_cities_for_expatriate_employees#Mercer_surveys" title="List of most expensive cities for expatriate employees">city rankings of cost of living for expatriate employees</a>, São Paulo is now among the ten most expensive cities in the world, ranking 10th in 2011, up from 21st in 2010 and ahead of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luxury_brand" title="Luxury brand">Luxury brands</a> tend to concentrate their business in São Paulo. Because of the lack of department stores and multi-brand boutiques, <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">shopping malls</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Jardins" title="Jardins">Jardins</a> district attract most of the world's luxurious brands. Most of the international luxury brands can be found in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iguatemi_Empresa_de_Shopping_Centers" title="Iguatemi Empresa de Shopping Centers">Iguatemi</a>, Cidade Jardim or JK shopping malls or on the streets of <a href="/wiki/Rua_Oscar_Freire" title="Rua Oscar Freire">Oscar Freire</a>, Lorena or Haddock Lobo in the Jardins district. They are home of brands such as <a href="/wiki/Cartier_(jeweler)" title="Cartier (jeweler)">Cartier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chanel" title="Chanel">Chanel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dior" title="Dior">Dior</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Armani" title="Giorgio Armani">Giorgio Armani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gucci" title="Gucci">Gucci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Vuitton" title="Louis Vuitton">Louis Vuitton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Jacobs" title="Marc Jacobs">Marc Jacobs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiffany_%26_Co" title="Tiffany &amp; Co">Tiffany &amp; Co</a>. Cidade Jardim was opened in São Paulo in 2008, it is a 45,000-square-meter (484,376-square-foot) mall, landscaped with trees and greenery scenario, with a focus on Brazilian brands but also home to international luxury brands such as <a href="/wiki/Herm%C3%A8s" title="Hermès">Hermès</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Choo" title="Jimmy Choo">Jimmy Choo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Pucci" title="Emilio Pucci">Pucci</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carolina_Herrera_(fashion_designer)" title="Carolina Herrera (fashion designer)">Carolina Herrera</a>. Opened in 2012, JK shopping mall has brought to Brazil brands that were not present in the country before such as Goyard, Tory Burch, Llc., <a href="/wiki/Prada" title="Prada">Prada</a>, and Miu Miu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Iguatemi_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Iguatemi São Paulo">Iguatemi</a> Faria Lima, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avenida_Brigadeiro_Faria_Lima" title="Avenida Brigadeiro Faria Lima">Faria Lima Avenue</a>, is Brazil's oldest mall, opened in 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jardins" title="Jardins">Jardins</a> neighborhood is regarded among the most sophisticated places in town, with upscale restaurants and hotels. The New York Times once compared Oscar Freire Street to <a href="/wiki/Rodeo_Drive" title="Rodeo Drive">Rodeo Drive</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> In Jardins there are luxury car dealers. One of the world's best restaurants as elected by The World's 50 Best Restaurants Award, D.O.M.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> is there.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Brazil" title="Tourism in Brazil">Tourism in Brazil</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ibirapuera,_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_(biennale)_07.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG/220px-Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG/330px-Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG/440px-Ibirapuera%2C_Pavilh%C3%A3o_Ciccillo_Matarazzo_%28biennale%29_07.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Art_Biennial" title="São Paulo Art Biennial">São Paulo Art Biennial</a>, the second oldest art biennial in the world after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venice_Biennial" title="Venice Biennial">Venice Biennial</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1496" data-file-width="2256" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG/220px-Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG/330px-Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG/440px-Sao_Paulo_-_Mercado_Municipal.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">The interior of the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Market_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Municipal Market of São Paulo">Municipal Market of São Paulo</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Large hotel chains whose target audience is the corporate traveler are in the city. São Paulo is home to 75% of the country's leading business fairs. The city also promotes one of the most important fashion weeks in the world, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Fashion_Week" title="São Paulo Fashion Week">São Paulo Fashion Week</a>, established in 1996 under the name Morumbi Fashion Brasil, is the largest and most important fashion event in Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Besides, the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Gay_Pride_Parade" title="São Paulo Gay Pride Parade">São Paulo Gay Pride Parade</a>, held since 1997 on <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">Paulista Avenue</a> is the event that attracts more tourists to the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup>
</p><p>The annual March For Jesus is a large gathering of Christians from Protestant churches throughout Brazil, with São Paulo police reporting participation in the range of 350,000 in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> In addition, São Paulo hosts the annual São Paulo Pancake Cook-Off in which chefs from across Brazil and the world participate in competitions based on the cooking of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pancakes" title="Pancakes">pancakes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cultural tourism also has relevance to the city, especially when considering the international events in the metropolis, such as the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Art_Biennial" title="São Paulo Art Biennial">São Paulo Art Biennial</a>, that attracted almost 1 million people in 2004.
</p><p>The city has a nightlife that is considered one of the best in the country, and is an international hub of highly active and diverse <a href="/wiki/Nightlife" title="Nightlife">nightlife</a> with <a href="/wiki/Bar_(establishment)" title="Bar (establishment)">bars</a>, dance bars and <a href="/wiki/Nightclub" title="Nightclub">nightclubs</a> staying open well past midnight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> There are cinemas, theaters, museums, and cultural centers. The <a href="/wiki/Rua_Oscar_Freire" title="Rua Oscar Freire">Rua Oscar Freire</a> was named one of the eight most luxurious streets in the world, according to the Mystery Shopping International,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oscar_Freire_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oscar_Freire-160">[160]</a></sup> and São Paulo the 25th "most expensive city" of the planet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the International Congress &amp; Convention Association, São Paulo ranks first among the cities that host international events in <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> and the 12th in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> According to a study by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MasterCard" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a> in 130 cities around the world, São Paulo was the third most visited destination in Latin America (behind <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>) with 2.4 million foreign travelers, who spent US$2.9 billion in 2013 (the highest among the cities in the region). In 2014, <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> ranked nightlife São Paulo as the fourth best in the world, behind <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ibiza" title="Ibiza">Ibiza</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup>
</p><p>The cuisine of the region is a tourist attraction. The city has 62 cuisines across 12,000 restaurants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> During the 10th International Congress of Gastronomy, Hospitality and Tourism (Cihat) conducted in 1997, the city received the title of "World Gastronomy Capital" from a commission formed by 43 nations' representatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1408px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" title="Panoramic view of the city at night from Ibirapuera Park"><img alt="" data-file-height="758" data-file-width="5616" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Panorama_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/1400px-Panorama_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Panorama_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/2100px-Panorama_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Panorama_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/2800px-Panorama_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 2x" width="1400"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" title="File:Panorama de São Paulo.jpg"> </a></div>Panoramic view of the city at night from <a href="/wiki/Ibirapuera_Park" title="Ibirapuera Park">Ibirapuera Park</a></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_infrastructure">Urban infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Urban infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CENU,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brasil_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2775" data-file-width="4360" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/CENU%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-CENU%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/CENU%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-CENU%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/CENU%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-CENU%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CENU,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brasil_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Oct%C3%A1vio_Frias_de_Oliveira_Bridge" title="Octávio Frias de Oliveira Bridge">Octávio Frias de Oliveira Bridge</a> aside of <a href="/wiki/Centro_Empresarial_Na%C3%A7%C3%B5es_Unidas" title="Centro Empresarial Nações Unidas">Centro Empresarial Nações Unidas</a></div></div></div>
<p>Since the beginning of the 20th century, São Paulo has been one of the main economic centers of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>. With the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWI" title="WWI">First</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWII" title="WWII">Second World Wars</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, coffee exports to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> were heavily affected, forcing the rich coffee growers to invest in the industrial activities that would make São Paulo the largest industrial center in Brazil. The new job vacancies contributed to attract a significant number of immigrants (mainly from Italy)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Italian_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Italian-166">[166]</a></sup> and migrants, especially from the Northeastern states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Causas_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-Causas-167">[167]</a></sup> From a population of only 32.000 people in 1880, São Paulo now has 8.5 million inhabitants in 1980. The rapid population growth has brought many problems for the city.
</p><p>São Paulo is practically all served by the water supply network. The city consumes an average of 221 liters of water/inhabitant/day while the UN recommends the consumption of 110 liters/day. The water loss is 30.8%. However, between 11 and 12.8% of households do not have a sewage system, depositing waste in pits and ditches. Sixty percent of the sewage collected is treated. According to data from IBGE and Eletropaulo, the electricity grid serves almost 100% of households. The fixed telephony network is still precarious, with coverage of 67.2%. Household garbage collection covers all regions of the municipality but is still insufficient, reaching around 94% of the demand in districts such as <a href="/wiki/Parelheiros_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Parelheiros (district of São Paulo)">Parelheiros</a> and Perus. About 80% of the garbage produced daily by Paulistas is exported to other cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Caieiras" title="Caieiras">Caieiras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guarulhos" title="Guarulhos">Guarulhos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lixo_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-lixo-168">[168]</a></sup> Recycling accounts for about 1% of the 15,000 metric tons of waste produced daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lixo_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-lixo-168">[168]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_planning">Urban planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Urban planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Planet_Imagery.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1235" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Planet_Imagery.jpg/220px-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Planet_Imagery.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Planet_Imagery.jpg/330px-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Planet_Imagery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Planet_Imagery.jpg/440px-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Planet_Imagery.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_Planet_Imagery.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Changes in urban fabrics in the region of <a href="/wiki/Jardins" title="Jardins">Jardins</a>: side by side, vertical areas and low houses</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Centro,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brazil_-_panoramio_(16).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Centro%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil_-_panoramio_%2816%29.jpg/220px-Centro%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil_-_panoramio_%2816%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Centro%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil_-_panoramio_%2816%29.jpg/330px-Centro%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil_-_panoramio_%2816%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Centro%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil_-_panoramio_%2816%29.jpg/440px-Centro%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil_-_panoramio_%2816%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Centro,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_-_State_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brazil_-_panoramio_(16).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Martinelli_Building" title="Martinelli Building">Martinelli Building</a> was the first <a href="/wiki/Skyscraper" title="Skyscraper">skyscraper</a> of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and the tallest until 1947</div></div></div>
<p>São Paulo has a myriad of urban fabrics. The original nuclei of the city are vertical, characterized by the presence of commercial buildings and services; And the peripheries are generally developed with two to four-story buildings – although such generalization certainly meets with exceptions in the fabric of the metropolis. Compared to other global cities (such as the island cities of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>), however, São Paulo is considered a "low-rise building" city. Its tallest buildings rarely reach forty stories, and the average residential building is twenty. Nevertheless, it is the fourth city in the world in quantity of buildings, according to the page specialized in research of data on buildings <i>Emporis Buildings</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> besides possessing what was considered until 2014 the tallest skyscraper of the country, the <a href="/wiki/Mirante_do_Vale" title="Mirante do Vale">Mirante do Vale</a>, also known as <i>Palácio Zarzur Kogan</i>, with 170 meters of height and 51 floors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>Such tissue heterogeneity, however, is not as predictable as the generic model can make us imagine. Some central regions of the city began to concentrate indigents, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drug_trafficking" title="Drug trafficking">drug trafficking</a>, street vending and <a href="/wiki/Prostitution" title="Prostitution">prostitution</a>, which encouraged the creation of new socio-economic centralities. The characterization of each region of the city also underwent several changes throughout the 20th century. With the relocation of industries to other cities or states, several areas that once housed factory sheds have become commercial or even residential areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Planejamento_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-Planejamento-171">[171]</a></sup>
</p><p>São Paulo has a history of actions, projects and plans related to urban planning that can be traced to the governments of Antonio da Silva Prado, Baron Duprat, Washington and Luis Francisco Prestes Maia. However, in general, the city was formed during the 20th century, growing from village to metropolis through a series of informal processes and irregular urban sprawl.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>Urban growth in São Paulo has followed three patterns since the beginning of the 20th century, according to urban historians: since the late 19th Century and until the 1940s, São Paulo was a condensed city in which different social groups lived in a small urban zone separated by type of housing; from the 1940s to the 1980s, São Paulo followed a model of center-periphery social segregation, in which the upper and middle-classes occupied central and modern areas while the poor moved towards precarious, self-built housing in the periphery; and from the 1980s onward, new transformations have brought the social classes closer together in spatial terms, but separated by walls and security technologies that seek to isolate the richer classes in the name of security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caldeira,_Teresa_P.R._2000._p._215_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caldeira,_Teresa_P.R._2000._p._215-173">[173]</a></sup> Thus, São Paulo differs considerably from other Brazilian cities such as <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goi%C3%A2nia" title="Goiânia">Goiânia</a>, whose initial expansion followed determinations by a plan, or a city like <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>, whose master plan had been fully developed prior to construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SP_from_Altino_Arantes_Building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4912" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/SP_from_Altino_Arantes_Building.jpg/220px-SP_from_Altino_Arantes_Building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/SP_from_Altino_Arantes_Building.jpg/330px-SP_from_Altino_Arantes_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/SP_from_Altino_Arantes_Building.jpg/440px-SP_from_Altino_Arantes_Building.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SP_from_Altino_Arantes_Building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The city view from <a href="/wiki/Altino_Arantes_Building" title="Altino Arantes Building">Altino Arantes Building</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:28_05_2019_Foto_do_dia_(47954186777).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2337" data-file-width="3506" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/28_05_2019_Foto_do_dia_%2847954186777%29.jpg/220px-28_05_2019_Foto_do_dia_%2847954186777%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/28_05_2019_Foto_do_dia_%2847954186777%29.jpg/330px-28_05_2019_Foto_do_dia_%2847954186777%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/28_05_2019_Foto_do_dia_%2847954186777%29.jpg/440px-28_05_2019_Foto_do_dia_%2847954186777%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:28_05_2019_Foto_do_dia_(47954186777).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pinheiros_River" title="Pinheiros River">Pinheiros River</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santo_Amaro_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Santo Amaro (district of São Paulo)">Santo Amaro district</a></div></div></div>
<p>The effectiveness of these plans has been seen by some planners and historians as questionable. Some of these scholars argue that such plans were produced exclusively for the benefit of the wealthier strata of the population while the working classes would be relegated to the traditional informal processes. In São Paulo until the mid-1950s, the plans were based on the idea of "demolish and rebuild", including former Mayor <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Prestes_Maia" title="Francisco Prestes Maia">Francisco Prestes Maia's</a> road plan for São Paulo (known as the Avenues Plan) or <a href="/wiki/Saturnino_de_Brito" title="Saturnino de Brito">Saturnino de Brito's</a> plan for the Tietê River. The Plan of the Avenues was implemented during the 1920s and sought to build large avenues connecting the city center with the outskirts. This plan included renewing the commercial city center, leading to real estate speculation and gentrification of several downtown neighborhoods. The plan also led to the expansion of bus services, which would soon replace the trolley as the preliminary transportation system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> This contributed to the outwards expansion of São Paulo and the peripherization of poorer residents. Peripheral neighborhoods were usually unregulated and consisted mainly of self-built single-family houses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caldeira,_Teresa_P.R._2000._p._215_173-1"><a href="#cite_note-Caldeira,_Teresa_P.R._2000._p._215-173">[173]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1968 the Urban Development Plan proposed the Basic Plan for Integrated Development of São Paulo, under the administration of Figueiredo Ferraz. The main result was zoning laws. It lasted until 2004 when the Basic Plan was replaced by the current Master Plan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> That zoning, adopted in 1972, designated "Z1" areas (<a href="/wiki/Residential_area" title="Residential area">residential areas</a> designed for elites) and "Z3" (a "mixed zone" lacking clear definitions about their characteristics). Zoning encouraged the growth of suburbs with minimal control and major speculation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> After the 1970s peripheral lot regulation increased and infrastructure in the periphery improved, driving land prices up. The poorest and the newcomers now could not purchase their lot and build their house, and were forced to look for a housing alternative. As a result, <a href="/wiki/Favela" title="Favela">favelas</a> and precarious tenements (cortiços) appeared.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> These housing types were often closer to the city's center: favelas could sprawl in any unused terrain (often dangerous or unsanitary) and decaying or abandoned buildings for tenements were abundant inside the city. Favelas went back into the urban perimeter, occupying the small lots not yet occupied by urbanization – alongside polluted rivers, railways, or between bridges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> By 1993, 19.8% of São Paulo's population lived in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Favelas" title="Favelas">favelas</a>, compared to 5.2% in 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Today, it is estimated that 2.1 million Paulistas live in favelas, which represents about 11% of the metropolitan area's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:908px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_da_cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" title="Panoramic view of Central Zone of São Paulo from Italy Building"><img alt="" data-file-height="2395" data-file-width="10155" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Panorama_da_cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/900px-Panorama_da_cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Panorama_da_cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/1350px-Panorama_da_cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Panorama_da_cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/1800px-Panorama_da_cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 2x" width="900"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_da_cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" title="File:Panorama da cidade de São Paulo.jpg"> </a></div>Panoramic view of <a href="/wiki/Central_Zone_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Central Zone of São Paulo">Central Zone of São Paulo</a> from <a href="/wiki/Edif%C3%ADcio_It%C3%A1lia" title="Edifício Itália">Italy Building</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Transport in São Paulo">Transport in São Paulo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Brazil" title="Transport in Brazil">Transport in Brazil</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:448px;max-width:448px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Movimento_nas_rodovias,_Imigrantes,_Anhanguera_e_Bandeirantes_no_feriado_prolongado._Dia_23_05_2020_Local_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_SP_Foto_Governo_do_Estado_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo._(49927076523).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="5472" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Movimento_nas_rodovias%2C_Imigrantes%2C_Anhanguera_e_Bandeirantes_no_feriado_prolongado._Dia_23_05_2020_Local_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_SP_Foto_Governo_do_Estado_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo._%2849927076523%29.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Movimento_nas_rodovias%2C_Imigrantes%2C_Anhanguera_e_Bandeirantes_no_feriado_prolongado._Dia_23_05_2020_Local_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_SP_Foto_Governo_do_Estado_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo._%2849927076523%29.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Movimento_nas_rodovias%2C_Imigrantes%2C_Anhanguera_e_Bandeirantes_no_feriado_prolongado._Dia_23_05_2020_Local_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_SP_Foto_Governo_do_Estado_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo._%2849927076523%29.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Rodovia_dos_Bandeirantes" title="Rodovia dos Bandeirantes">Bandeirantes Highway</a>/SP-348</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG/220px-Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG/330px-Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG/440px-Rodoanel_Mario_Covas7.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Rodoanel_M%C3%A1rio_Covas" title="Rodoanel Mário Covas">Mario Covas Beltway</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Automobiles are the main means to get into the city. In March 2011, more than 7 million vehicles were registered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Heavy traffic is common on the city's main avenues and <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">traffic jams</a> are relatively common on its highways.
</p><p>The city is crossed by 10 major motorways: <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Presidente_Dutra" title="Rodovia Presidente Dutra">President Dutra Highwa</a>/BR-116 (connects São Paulo to the east and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ordinal_direction" title="Ordinal direction">north-east</a> of the country); Régis Bittencourt Highway/BR-116 (connects São Paulo to the south of the country); <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Fern%C3%A3o_Dias" title="Rodovia Fernão Dias">Fernão Dias Highway</a>/BR-381 (connects São Paulo to the north of the country); <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Anchieta" title="Rodovia Anchieta">Anchieta Highwa</a>/SP-150 (connects São Paulo to the ocean coast); <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_dos_Imigrantes" title="Rodovia dos Imigrantes">Immigrants Highway</a>/SP-150 (connects São Paulo to the ocean coast); <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Castelo_Branco" title="Rodovia Castelo Branco">President Castelo Branco Highway</a>/SP-280 (connects São Paulo to the west and north-west of the country); <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Raposo_Tavares" title="Rodovia Raposo Tavares">Raposo Tavares Highway</a>/SP-270 (connects São Paulo to the west of the country); <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Anhanguera" title="Rodovia Anhanguera">Anhanguera Highway</a>/SP-330 (connects São Paulo to the north-west of the country, including its capital city); <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_dos_Bandeirantes" title="Rodovia dos Bandeirantes">Bandeirantes Highway</a>/SP-348 (connects São Paulo to the north-west of the country); <a href="/wiki/Rodovia_Ayrton_Senna" title="Rodovia Ayrton Senna">Ayrton Senna Highway</a>/SP-70 (named after Brazilian legendary <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> driver <a href="/wiki/Ayrton_Senna" title="Ayrton Senna">Ayrton Senna</a>, the motorway connects São Paulo to east locations of the state, as well as the north coast of the state). 
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Rodoanel_M%C3%A1rio_Covas" title="Rodoanel Mário Covas">Rodoanel Mário Covas</a> (official designation SP-021) is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beltway" title="Beltway">beltway</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater São Paulo">Greater São Paulo</a>. Upon its completion, it will have a length of 177 km (110 mi), with a radius of approximately 23 km (14 mi) from the geographical center of the city. It was named after Mário Covas, who was mayor of the city of São Paulo (1983–1985) and a state governor (1994-1998/1998-2001) until his death from cancer. It is a controlled access highway with a speed limit of 100 km/h (62 mph) under normal weather and traffic circumstances. The west, south and east parts are completed, and the north part, which will close the beltway, is due in 2022 and is being built by DERSA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1772" data-file-width="2691" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg/220px-Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg/330px-Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg/440px-Aeroporto_de_Congonhas_-_Aeronaves.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congonhas-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Airport" title="Congonhas-São Paulo Airport">Congonhas Airport</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3194" data-file-width="5022" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg/220px-Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg/330px-Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg/440px-Terminal_3_de_Guarulhos.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo%E2%80%93Guarulhos_International_Airport" title="São Paulo–Guarulhos International Airport">São Paulo–Guarulhos International Airport</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>São Paulo has two main airports, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo%E2%80%93Guarulhos_International_Airport" title="São Paulo–Guarulhos International Airport">São Paulo–Guarulhos International Airport</a> for international flights and national hub, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congonhas-S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Airport" title="Congonhas-São Paulo Airport">Congonhas-São Paulo Airport</a> for domestic and regional flights. Another airport, the <a href="/wiki/Campo_de_Marte_Airport" title="Campo de Marte Airport">Campo de Marte Airport</a>, serves private jets and light aircraft. The three airports together moved more than 58.000.000 passengers in 2015, making São Paulo one of the top 15 busiest in the world, by number of air passenger movements. The region of Greater São Paulo is also served by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viracopos-Campinas_International_Airport" title="Viracopos-Campinas International Airport">Viracopos-Campinas International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_dos_Campos_Airport" title="São José dos Campos Airport">São José dos Campos Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jundia%C3%AD_Airport" title="Jundiaí Airport">Jundiaí Airport</a>.
</p><p>Congonhas Airport operates flights mainly to Rio de Janeiro, Porto Alegre, Belo Horizonte and Brasília. Built in the 1930s, it was designed to handle the increasing demand for flights, in the fastest growing city in the world. Located in Campo Belo District, Congonhas Airport is close to the three main city's financial districts: <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">Paulista Avenue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brigadeiro_Faria_Lima_Avenue" title="Brigadeiro Faria Lima Avenue">Brigadeiro Faria Lima Avenue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Engenheiro_Lu%C3%ADs_Carlos_Berrini_Avenue" title="Engenheiro Luís Carlos Berrini Avenue">Engenheiro Luís Carlos Berrini Avenue</a>.
</p><p>The São Paulo–Guarulhos International, also known as "Cumbica", is 25 km (16 mi) north-east of the city center, in the neighboring city of <a href="/wiki/Guarulhos" title="Guarulhos">Guarulhos</a>. Every day nearly 110.000 people pass through the airport, which connects Brazil to 36 countries around the world. 370 companies operate there, generating more than 53.000 jobs. The international airport is connected to the metropolitan rail system, with <a href="/wiki/Line_13_(CPTM)" title="Line 13 (CPTM)">Line 13 (CPTM)</a>.
</p><p>Campo de Marte is in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santana_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Santana (São Paulo)">Santana</a> district, the northern <a href="/wiki/Zoning" title="Zoning">zone</a> of São Paulo. The airport handles private flights and air shuttles, including <a href="/wiki/Air_taxi" title="Air taxi">air taxi</a> firms. Opened in 1935, Campo de Marte is the base for the largest helicopter fleet in Brazil and the world's, ahead of New York and Tokyo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> This airport is the home base of the State Civil Police Air Tactical Unit, the State Military Police Radio Patrol Unit and the São Paulo Flying Club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup>
From this airport, passengers can take advantage of some 350 remote helipads and heliports to bypass heavy road traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_rail">Urban rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Urban rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="São Paulo Metro">São Paulo Metro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Companhia_Paulista_de_Trens_Metropolitanos" title="Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos">Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos</a></div>
<p>São Paulo has a <a href="/wiki/Urban_rail_transit" title="Urban rail transit">urban rail transit</a> system (<a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="São Paulo Metro">São Paulo Metro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Companhia_Paulista_de_Trens_Metropolitanos" title="Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos">CPTM</a>) that serves 184 stations and has 377 km (234 mi) of track,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> forming the largest <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo#Rail_transport" title="Transport in São Paulo">metropolitan rail transport network</a> of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> The underground and urban railway lines together carry some 7 million people on an average weekday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner"
