class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_rail" title="Urban rail">urban rail</a> network of the city (<a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="São Paulo Metro">São Paulo Metro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Companhia_Paulista_de_Trens_Metropolitanos" title="Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos">CPTM</a>)</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:179px;max-width:179px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:117px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monotrilho_SP_(3).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Monotrilho_SP_%283%29.jpg/177px-Monotrilho_SP_%283%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Monotrilho_SP_%283%29.jpg/266px-Monotrilho_SP_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Monotrilho_SP_%283%29.jpg/354px-Monotrilho_SP_%283%29.jpg 2x" width="177"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Monorail" title="Monorail">Monorail</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Line_15_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro)" title="Line 15 (São Paulo Metro)">Line 15 (Silver)</a> of the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="São Paulo Metro">São Paulo Metro</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:119px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Metro_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_3_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="797" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Metro_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_3_%28cropped%29.jpg/180px-Metro_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_3_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Metro_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_3_%28cropped%29.jpg/270px-Metro_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_3_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Metro_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_3_%28cropped%29.jpg/360px-Metro_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_3_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Train of the <a href="/wiki/Line_4_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro)" title="Line 4 (São Paulo Metro)">Line 4 (Yellow)</a> of the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="São Paulo Metro">São Paulo Metro</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:176px;max-width:176px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:119px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz._(29024398597).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="4160" data-file-width="6051" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz._%2829024398597%29.jpg/174px-Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz._%2829024398597%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz._%2829024398597%29.jpg/261px-Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz._%2829024398597%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz._%2829024398597%29.jpg/348px-Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_da_Luz._%2829024398597%29.jpg 2x" width="174"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Train of the <a href="/wiki/Companhia_Paulista_de_Trens_Metropolitanos" title="Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos">CPTM</a> at <a href="/wiki/Luz_Station" title="Luz Station">Luz Station</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro" title="São Paulo Metro">São Paulo Metro</a> operates 104 kilometers (65 mi) of <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> system, with six lines in operation, serving 91 stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spmetro_about_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-spmetro_about-190">[190]</a></sup> In 2015, the metro reached the mark of 11.5 million passengers per mile of line, 15% higher than in 2008, when 10 million users were taken per mile. It is the largest concentration of people in a single transport system in the world, according to the company. The company ViaQuatro, a <a href="/wiki/Concession_(contract)" title="Concession (contract)">private concessionaire</a>, operates the <a href="/wiki/Line_4_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro)" title="Line 4 (São Paulo Metro)">Line 4</a> of the system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> In 2014, the São Paulo Metro was elected the best metro system in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Line_15_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro)" title="Line 15 (São Paulo Metro)">Line 15 (Silver)</a> of the São Paulo Metro is the first mass-transit <a href="/wiki/Monorail" title="Monorail">monorail</a> of the South America and the first system in the world to use the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bombardier_Innovia_Monorail" title="Bombardier Innovia Monorail">Bombardier Innovia Monorail</a> 300. When fully completed will be the largest and highest capacity monorail system in the Americas and second worldwide, only behind to the <a href="/wiki/Chongqing_Rail_Transit" title="Chongqing Rail Transit">Chongqing Monorail</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Companhia_Paulista_de_Trens_Metropolitanos" title="Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos">Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos</a> (CPTM, or "Paulista Company of Metropolitan Trains") railway add 273.0 km (169.6 mi) of <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">commuter rail</a>, with seven lines and 94 stations. The system carries about 2.8 million passengers a day. On 8 June 2018, CPTM set a weekday ridership record with 3,096,035 trips.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Line_13_(CPTM)" title="Line 13 (CPTM)">Line 13 (Jade)</a> of the CPTM connects São Paulo to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo%E2%80%93Guarulhos_International_Airport" title="São Paulo–Guarulhos International Airport">São Paulo–Guarulhos International Airport</a>, in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Guarulhos" title="Guarulhos">Guarulhos</a>, the first major international airport in South America to be directly served by train.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/CCR_S.A." title="CCR S.A.">CCR Group</a> (through the <a href="/wiki/ViaQuatro" title="ViaQuatro">ViaQuatro</a> and <a href="/wiki/ViaMobilidade" title="ViaMobilidade">ViaMobilidade</a> concessionaires) operates subway lines <a href="/wiki/Line_4_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro)" title="Line 4 (São Paulo Metro)">4–Yellow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Line_5_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Metro)" title="Line 5 (São Paulo Metro)">5–Lilac</a>, in addition to managing (through the ViaMobilidade concessionaire) lines <a href="/wiki/Line_8_(CPTM)" title="Line 8 (CPTM)">8-Diamond</a> and <a href="/wiki/Line_9_(CPTM)" title="Line 9 (CPTM)">9-Emerald</a> of the metropolitan train system. Metro and metropolitan train networks transport an average of nearly 7 million people a day, while another 2 million passengers are transported by EMTU buses daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup>
</p><p>The two major São Paulo <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railway_stations" title="Railway stations">railway stations</a> are Luz and Júlio Prestes in the Luz/Campos Eliseos region. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_J%C3%BAlio_Prestes" title="Estação Júlio Prestes">Julio Prestes Station</a> connected Southwest São Paulo State and Northern <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paraná (state)">Paraná</a> State to São Paulo City. Agricultural products were transferred to Luz Station from which they headed to the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and overseas. Júlio Prestes stopped transporting passengers through the Sorocabana or FEPASA lines and now only has metro service. Due to its acoustics and interior beauty, surrounded by Greek revival columns, part of the rebuilt station was transformed into the São Paulo Hall.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Luz_Station" title="Luz Station">Luz Station</a> was built in Britain and assembled in Brazil. It has an underground station and is still active with metro lines that link São Paulo to the Greater São Paulo region to the East and the Campinas Metropolitan region in <a href="/wiki/Jundia%C3%AD" title="Jundiaí">Jundiaí</a> in the western part of the State. Luz Station is surrounded by important <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultural</a> institutions such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pinacoteca_do_Estado" title="Pinacoteca do Estado">Pinacoteca do Estado</a>, The Museu de Arte Sacra on Tiradentes Avenue and Jardim da Luz, among others. It is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Estrada_de_Ferro_Santos-Jundia%C3%AD" title="Estrada de Ferro Santos-Jundiaí">Santos-Jundiaí line</a> which historically transported <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">international immigrants</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Santos" title="Port of Santos">Port of Santos</a> to São Paulo and the coffee plantation lands in the Western region of <a href="/wiki/Campinas" title="Campinas">Campinas</a>. São Paulo has no <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tram</a> lines, although trams were common in the first half of the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">Buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/SPTrans" title="SPTrans">SPTrans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Empresa_Metropolitana_de_Transportes_Urbanos_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Empresa Metropolitana de Transportes Urbanos de São Paulo">Empresa Metropolitana de Transportes Urbanos de São Paulo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Trolleybuses in São Paulo">Trolleybuses in São Paulo</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:448px;max-width:448px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Himalaia_-_4_1510_-_Flickr_-_Rafael_Delazari.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1644" data-file-width="2192" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Himalaia_-_4_1510_-_Flickr_-_Rafael_Delazari.jpg/220px-Himalaia_-_4_1510_-_Flickr_-_Rafael_Delazari.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Himalaia_-_4_1510_-_Flickr_-_Rafael_Delazari.jpg/330px-Himalaia_-_4_1510_-_Flickr_-_Rafael_Delazari.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Himalaia_-_4_1510_-_Flickr_-_Rafael_Delazari.jpg/440px-Himalaia_-_4_1510_-_Flickr_-_Rafael_Delazari.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">São Paulo has <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Trolleybuses in São Paulo">two independent trolleybus systems</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-janes2011_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-janes2011-198">[198]</a></sup></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg/220px-Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg/330px-Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg/440px-Terminal_Rodovi%C3%A1rio_Tiet%C3%AA.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_Bus_Terminal" title="Tietê Bus Terminal">Tietê Bus Terminal</a>, the 2nd largest <a href="/wiki/Bus_station" title="Bus station">bus terminal</a> in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_Bus_Terminal" title="Port Authority Bus Terminal">PABT</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tietê_Bus_Terminal_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tietê_Bus_Terminal-199">[199]</a></sup></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Bus transport (government and private) is composed of 17,000 buses (including about 290 <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolley buses</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juts2009_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-juts2009-200">[200]</a></sup> The traditional system of informal transport (dab vans) was later reorganized and legalized. The <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybus</a> systems provide a portion of the <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transport</a> service in <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater São Paulo">Greater São Paulo</a> with two independent netwoeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moraes1999_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-moraes1999-201">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-janes2011_198-1"><a href="#cite_note-janes2011-198">[198]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/SPTrans" title="SPTrans">SPTrans</a> (São Paulo Transportes) system opened in 1949 and serves the city of São Paulo, while the <a href="/wiki/Empresa_Metropolitana_de_Transportes_Urbanos_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Empresa Metropolitana de Transportes Urbanos de São Paulo">Empresa Metropolitana de Transportes Urbanos de São Paulo</a> (EMTU) system opened in 1988 and serves suburban areas to the southeast of the city proper. Worldwide, São Paulo is one of only two metropolitan areas possessing two independent trolleybus systems, the other being <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Naples" title="Trolleybuses in Naples">Naples, Italy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-janes2011_198-2"><a href="#cite_note-janes2011-198">[198]</a></sup>
</p><p>São Paulo <a href="/wiki/Tiet%C3%AA_Bus_Terminal" title="Tietê Bus Terminal">Tietê Bus Terminal</a> the second largest <a href="/wiki/Bus_station" title="Bus station">bus terminal</a> in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_Bus_Terminal" title="Port Authority Bus Terminal">PABT</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tietê_Bus_Terminal_199-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tietê_Bus_Terminal-199">[199]</a></sup> It serves localities across the nation, with the exception of the states of <a href="/wiki/Amazonas_(Brazilian_state)" title="Amazonas (Brazilian state)">Amazonas</a>, Roraima and <a href="/wiki/Amap%C3%A1" title="Amapá">Amapá</a>. Routes to 1,010 cities in five countries (Brazil, Argentina, Chile, Uruguay and Paraguay) are available. It connects to all regional airports and a <a href="/wiki/Carpool" title="Carpool">ride sharing</a> automobile service to <a href="/wiki/Santos,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Santos, São Paulo">Santos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tietê_Bus_Terminal_199-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tietê_Bus_Terminal-199">[199]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Palmeiras-Barra_Funda_Intermodal_Terminal" title="Palmeiras-Barra Funda Intermodal Terminal">Palmeiras-Barra Funda Intermodal Terminal</a> is much smaller and is connected to the Palmeiras-Barra Funda metro and Palmeiras-Barra Funda CPTM stations. It serves the southwestern cities of <a href="/wiki/Sorocaba" title="Sorocaba">Sorocaba</a>, Itapetininga, Itu, Botucatu, <a href="/wiki/Bauru" title="Bauru">Bauru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADlia" title="Marília">Marília</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ja%C3%BA" title="Jaú">Jaú</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avar%C3%A9,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Avaré, São Paulo">Avaré</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piraju" title="Piraju">Piraju</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_do_Rio_Pardo" title="Santa Cruz do Rio Pardo">Santa Cruz do Rio Pardo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ipaussu" title="Ipaussu">Ipaussu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chavantes" title="Chavantes">Chavantes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ourinhos" title="Ourinhos">Ourinhos</a> (on the border with <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paraná (state)">Paraná</a> State). It also serves <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_do_Rio_Preto" title="São José do Rio Preto">São José do Rio Preto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ara%C3%A7atuba" title="Araçatuba">Araçatuba</a> and other small towns on the northwest of São Paulo State.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Brazil" title="Music of Brazil">Music of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:372px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6375" data-file-width="17895" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/370px-Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/555px-Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg/740px-Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg 2x" width="370"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Webysther_20150501201754_-_Interior_Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Sala São Paulo">Sala São Paulo</a>, the home of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_State_Symphony" title="São Paulo State Symphony">São Paulo State Symphony</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Adoniran_Barbosa" title="Adoniran Barbosa">Adoniran Barbosa</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Samba" title="Samba">samba</a> singer and composer who became successful during São Paulo's early radio era. Born in 1912 in the town of <a href="/wiki/Valinhos" title="Valinhos">Valinhos</a>, Barbosa was known as the "composer to the masses", particularly Italian immigrants living in the quarters of Bela Vista, also known as "Bexiga" and Brás, as well as those who lived in the city's many 'cortiços' or tenements. His songs drew from the life of urban workers, the unemployed and those who lived on the edge. His first big hit was "Saudosa Maloca" ("Shanty of Fond Memories" – 1951), wherein three homeless friends recall with nostalgia their improvised shanty home, which was torn down by the landowner to make room for a building. His 1964 <a href="/wiki/Trem_das_Onze" title="Trem das Onze">Trem das Onze</a> ("The 11 pm Train"), became one of the five best samba songs ever, the protagonist explains to his lover that he cannot stay any longer because he has to catch the last train to the <a href="/wiki/Ja%C3%A7an%C3%A3_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Jaçanã (district of São Paulo)">Jaçanã suburb</a>, for his mother will not sleep before he arrives home. Another important musician with a similar style is <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Vanzolini" title="Paulo Vanzolini">Paulo Vanzolini</a>. Vanzolini is a PhD in Biology and a part-time professional musician. He composed a song depicting a love murder scene in São Paulo called "Ronda".
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1232" data-file-width="1840" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg/220px-Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg/330px-Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg/440px-Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ibirapuera_Auditorium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ibirapuera_Auditorium" title="Ibirapuera Auditorium">Ibirapuera Auditorium</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tit%C3%A3s_post_2016_line_up.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tit%C3%A3s_post_2016_line_up.jpg/220px-Tit%C3%A3s_post_2016_line_up.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tit%C3%A3s_post_2016_line_up.jpg/330px-Tit%C3%A3s_post_2016_line_up.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tit%C3%A3s_post_2016_line_up.jpg/440px-Tit%C3%A3s_post_2016_line_up.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tit%C3%A3s_post_2016_line_up.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tit%C3%A3s" title="Titãs">Titãs</a> live at the Montevideo Rock 2018.</div></div></div>
<p>In the late 1960s, a psychedelic rock band called <a href="/wiki/Os_Mutantes" title="Os Mutantes">Os Mutantes</a> became popular. Their success is related to that of other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropicalismo" title="Tropicalismo">tropicalia</a> musicians. The group was known as very <i>paulistanos</i> in its behavior and clothing. Os Mutantes released five albums before lead singer <a href="/wiki/Rita_Lee" title="Rita Lee">Rita Lee</a> departed in 1972 to join another group called <a href="/wiki/Tutti_Frutti_(Brazilian_band)" title="Tutti Frutti (Brazilian band)">Tutti Frutti</a>. Although initially known only in Brazil, Os Mutantes became successful abroad after the 1990s. In 2000, <i><a href="/wiki/Tecnicolor" title="Tecnicolor">Tecnicolor</a></i>, an album recorded in the early 1970s in English by the band, was released with artwork designed by <a href="/wiki/Sean_Lennon" title="Sean Lennon">Sean Lennon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early 1980s, a band called <i><a href="/wiki/Ultraje_a_Rigor" title="Ultraje a Rigor">Ultraje a Rigor</a></i> (Elegant Outrage) emerged. They played a simple and irreverent style of rock. The lyrics depicted the changes in society and culture that Brazilian society was experiencing. A late punk and garage scene became strong in the 1980s, perhaps associated with the gloomy scenario of unemployment during an extended recession. Bands originating from this movement include <a href="/wiki/Ira!" title="Ira!">Ira!</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tit%C3%A3s" title="Titãs">Titãs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ratos_de_Por%C3%A3o" title="Ratos de Porão">Ratos de Porão</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inocentes" title="Inocentes">Inocentes</a>. In the 1990s, <a href="/wiki/Drum_and_bass" title="Drum and bass">drum and bass</a> arose as another musical movement in São Paulo, with artists such as <a href="/wiki/DJ_Marky" title="DJ Marky">DJ Marky</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Patife" title="DJ Patife">DJ Patife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xerxes_de_Oliveira" title="Xerxes de Oliveira">XRS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drumagick" title="Drumagick">Drumagick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fernanda_Porto" title="Fernanda Porto">Fernanda Porto</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> Many <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a> bands also originated in São Paulo, such as <a href="/wiki/Angra_(band)" title="Angra (band)">Angra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Project46" title="Project46">Project46</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torture_Squad" title="Torture Squad">Torture Squad</a>, Korzus and <a href="/wiki/Dr._Sin" title="Dr. Sin">Dr. Sin</a>. Famous electro-pop band <a href="/wiki/CSS_(band)" title="CSS (band)">Cansei de Ser Sexy</a>, or CSS (Portuguese for "tired of being sexy") also has its origins in the city.
</p><p>Many of the most important classical Brazilian living composers, such as <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Amaral_Vieira" title="José Carlos Amaral Vieira">Amaral Vieira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osvaldo_Lacerda" title="Osvaldo Lacerda">Osvaldo Lacerda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edson_Zampronha" title="Edson Zampronha">Edson Zampronha</a>, were born and live in São Paulo. Local <a href="/wiki/Baritone" title="Baritone">baritone</a> <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Szot" title="Paulo Szot">Paulo Szot</a> has won international acclaim performing for six consecutive seasons at The Metropolitan Opera, La Scala and Opera de Paris, among others; and The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">Tony Award</a> for best actor in a musical for his performance in a 2008 revival of <i><a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_(musical)" title="South Pacific (musical)">South Pacific</a></i>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orquestra_Sinf%C3%B4nica_do_Estado_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Orquestra Sinfônica do Estado de São Paulo">São Paulo State Symphony</a> is one of the world's outstanding orchestras; their artistic director beginning in 2012 is the noted American conductor <a href="/wiki/Marin_Alsop" title="Marin Alsop">Marin Alsop</a>. In 1952, <a href="/wiki/Heitor_Villa-Lobos" title="Heitor Villa-Lobos">Heitor Villa-Lobos</a> wrote his Symphony Number 10 ('Ameríndia') for the 400th anniversary of São Paulo: an allegorical, historical and religious account of the city told through the eyes of its founder <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Anchieta" title="José de Anchieta">José de Anchieta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup>
</p><p>São Paulo's opera houses are: <a href="/wiki/Theatro_Municipal_(S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Theatro Municipal (São Paulo)">São Paulo Municipal Theater</a>, Theatro São Pedro and Alfa Theater, for the symphonic concerts there is the <a href="/wiki/Sala_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Sala São Paulo">Sala São Paulo</a>, the latter being the headquarters of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OSESP" title="OSESP">OSESP</a>, an orchestra. The city hosts several music halls. The main ones are: Citibank Hall, HSBC Music Hall, Olympia, Via Funchal, Villa Country, Arena Anhembi and Espaco das Américas. The <a href="/wiki/Anhembi_Sambadrome" title="Anhembi Sambadrome">Anhembi Sambadrome</a> hosts musical presentations as well, in addition to the <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Carnival of São Paulo">Carnival of São Paulo</a>. Other facilities include the new Praça das Artes, with the Municipal Conservatory of Music Chamber Hall and others venues, like, Cultura Artistica, Teatro Sérgio Cardoso with a venue for only dance performances and Herzog &amp; DeMeron's Centro Cultural Luz, for Ballet, Opera, theater and concerts, with three huge halls. The auditorium of the Latin-American Cultural Center, The Mozarteum, holds concerts through the year. Festivals as the <a href="/wiki/Virada_Cultural" title="Virada Cultural">Virada Cultural</a> (Cultural Overnight) happen once a year and holds hundreds of attractions spread throughout the city.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Virada.jpg" title="2007 Virada Cultural, in Downtown São Paulo"><img alt="" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="1990" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virada.jpg/800px-Virada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virada.jpg/1200px-Virada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virada.jpg/1600px-Virada.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virada.jpg" title="File:Virada.jpg"> </a></div>2007 <a href="/wiki/Virada_Cultural" title="Virada Cultural">Virada Cultural</a>, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Downtown São Paulo">Downtown São Paulo</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literature_of_Brazil" title="Literature of Brazil">Literature of Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_Mario_Andrade,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brasil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5118" data-file-width="5869" decoding="async" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Biblioteca_Mario_Andrade%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg/220px-Biblioteca_Mario_Andrade%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Biblioteca_Mario_Andrade%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg/330px-Biblioteca_Mario_Andrade%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Biblioteca_Mario_Andrade%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg/440px-Biblioteca_Mario_Andrade%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brasil.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_Mario_Andrade,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brasil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade_Library" title="Mário de Andrade Library">Mário de Andrade Library</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livraria_Cultura,_Avenida_Paulista,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brazil.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2549" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Livraria_Cultura%2C_Avenida_Paulista%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg/220px-Livraria_Cultura%2C_Avenida_Paulista%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Livraria_Cultura%2C_Avenida_Paulista%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg/330px-Livraria_Cultura%2C_Avenida_Paulista%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Livraria_Cultura%2C_Avenida_Paulista%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg/440px-Livraria_Cultura%2C_Avenida_Paulista%2C_S%C3%A3o_Paulo%2C_Brazil.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livraria_Cultura,_Avenida_Paulista,_S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brazil.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Livraria_Cultura" title="Livraria Cultura">Livraria Cultura</a></div></div></div>
<p>São Paulo was home to the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> missionaries in Brazil, in the early 16th century. They wrote reports to the Portuguese crown about the newly found land, the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">native peoples</a> and composed poetry and music for the <a href="/wiki/Catechism" title="Catechism">catechism</a>, creating the first written works from the area. The literary priests included <a href="/wiki/Manuel_da_N%C3%B3brega" title="Manuel da Nóbrega">Manuel da Nóbrega</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Anchieta" title="José de Anchieta">José de Anchieta</a>, living in or near the colony then called <i>Piratininga</i>. They also helped to register the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Tupi_language" title="Old Tupi language">Old Tupi language</a>, lexicon and its grammar.
In 1922, the Brazilian Modernist Movement, launched in São Paulo, began to achieve cultural independence. Brazil had gone through the same stages of development as the rest of Latin America, but its political and cultural <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a> came more gradually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup>
</p><p>Brazilian elite culture was originally strongly tied to <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Portugal" title="Culture of Portugal">Portugal</a>. Gradually writers developed a multi-ethnic body of work that was distinctively Brazilian. The presence of large numbers of former slaves added a distinctive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Africa" title="Ethnic groups of Africa">African</a> character to the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Brazil" title="Culture of Brazil">culture</a>. Subsequent infusions of immigrants of non-Portuguese origin broadened the range of influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Modernism_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-Modernism-206">[206]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_de_Andrade" title="Mário de Andrade">Mário de Andrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oswald_de_Andrade" title="Oswald de Andrade">Oswald de Andrade</a> were the prototypical modernists. With the urban poems of "Paulicéia Desvairada" and "Carefree Paulistan land" (1922), Mário de Andrade established the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_movement" title="Cultural movement">movement</a> in Brazil. His rhapsodic novel <i>Macunaíma</i> (1928), with its abundance of Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a>, represents the apex of <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">modernism</a>'s nationalist prose through its creation of an offbeat native <a href="/wiki/Hero" title="Hero">national hero</a>. Oswald de Andrade's experimental poetry, <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> prose, particularly the novel Serafim Ponte Grande (1933) and provocative manifestos exemplify the movement's break with tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Modernism_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-Modernism-206">[206]</a></sup>
</p><p>Modernist artists and writers chose the Municipal Theatre of São Paulo to launch their Modernist manifesto. The site happened to be a bastion of European culture with opera and classical music presentations from Germany, France, Austria and Italy. They defied the high society that frequented the venue and who insisted on speaking only foreign languages such as French, behaving as if Brazilian culture did not matter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Modernism_206-2"><a href="#cite_note-Modernism-206">[206]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theaters">Theaters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Theaters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many historians believe that the first theatrical performance in Brazil was held in São Paulo. The Portuguese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> missionary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Anchieta" title="José de Anchieta">José de Anchieta</a> (1534–1597) wrote short plays that were performed and watched by the Tupi–Guarani natives. In the second half of the 19th century a cultural, musical and theatrical life emerged. <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European ethnic groups</a> began holding performances in some of the state's rural cities. The most important period for the art in São Paulo was the 1940s. São Paulo had had a professional company, Teatro Brasileiro de Comédia, (Brazilian Theater of Comedy), along with others.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7210" data-file-width="11224" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg/220px-Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg/330px-Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg/440px-Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_Municipal_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_8.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipal_Theatre_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Municipal Theatre of São Paulo">Municipal Theatre of São Paulo</a></div></div></div>
<p>During the 1960s, major theater productions in São Paulo and Brazil were presented by two groups. Teatro de Arena began with a group of students from Escola de Arte Dramática (Drama <a href="/wiki/Art_school" title="Art school">Art School</a>), founded by Alfredo Mesquita, in 1948. In 1958, the group excelled with the play "Eles não usam black tie" by <a href="/wiki/Gianfrancesco_Guarnieri" title="Gianfrancesco Guarnieri">Gianfrancesco Guarnieri</a> which was the first in the history of the Brazilian drama to feature <a href="/wiki/Wage_labour" title="Wage labour">labor</a> <a href="/wiki/Laborer" title="Laborer">workers</a> as <a href="/wiki/Protagonist" title="Protagonist">protagonists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup>
</p><p>After the military coup of 1964, plays started focusing on <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brazil" title="History of Brazil">Brazilian history</a> (Zumbi, Tiradentes). Teatro de Arena and Teatro Oficina supported the democratic resistance during the <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military dictatorship</a> period, marked by its censorship. The Tropicalist movement began there. A number of plays represented <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">historic</a> moments, notably "O Rei da Vela", "Galileu Galilei" (1968), "Na Sela das Cidades" (1969) and "Gracias Señor" (1972).
</p><p>The district of Bixiga concentrates the greatest number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theater" title="Theater">theaters</a>, around 40 including the theaters that are closed for refurbishing or for other reasons, and small alternatives companies venues. Some of the most important are Renault, Brigadeiro, Zaccaro, <a href="/wiki/Bibi_Ferreira" title="Bibi Ferreira">Bibi Ferreira</a>, Maria della Costa, Ruth Escobar, Opera, TBC, Imprensa, Oficina, Àgora, Cacilda Becker, Sérgio Cardoso, do Bixiga, and Bandeirantes.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Webysther_20190304150324_-_Parque_da_Independ%C3%AAncia.jpg/330px-Webysther_20190304150324_-_Parque_da_Independ%C3%AAncia.jpg 1.5x, width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museu_Paulista" title="Museu Paulista">Ipiranga Museum</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Webysther_20150428132400_-_M%C3%A3o.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3106" data-file-width="4659" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Webysther_20150428132400_-_M%C3%A3o.jpg/220px-Webysther_20150428132400_-_M%C3%A3o.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Webysther_20150428132400_-_M%C3%A3o.jpg/330px-Webysther_20150428132400_-_M%C3%A3o.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Webysther_20150428132400_-_M%C3%A3o.jpg/440px-Webysther_20150428132400_-_M%C3%A3o.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Latin_America_Memorial" title="Latin America Memorial">Latin America Memorial</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MIS,_SP,_5.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/MIS%2C_SP%2C_5.JPG/220px-MIS%2C_SP%2C_5.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/MIS%2C_SP%2C_5.JPG/330px-MIS%2C_SP%2C_5.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/MIS%2C_SP%2C_5.JPG/440px-MIS%2C_SP%2C_5.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Museum_of_Image_and_Sound" title="São Paulo Museum of Image and Sound">São Paulo Museum of Image and Sound</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>São Paulo has many neighborhoods and buildings of historical value. The city has a large number of museums and art galleries. Among the museums in the city are <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Museum_of_Art" title="São Paulo Museum of Art">São Paulo Museum of Art</a> (MASP), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museu_Paulista" title="Museu Paulista">Ipiranga Museum</a>, the Museum of Sacred Art, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Museum of the Portuguese Language">Museum of the Portuguese Language</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pinacoteca_do_Estado_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Pinacoteca do Estado de São Paulo">Pinacoteca do Estado de São Paulo</a>, among other renowned institutions. It also houses one of the top five zoos in the world, the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Zoo" title="São Paulo Zoo">São Paulo Zoo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ipiranga_Museum" title="Ipiranga Museum">Ipiranga Museum</a> is the first monument built to preserve the memory of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Brazilian Declaration of Independence">Independence of Brazil</a>, opened on 7 September 1895, with the name of Natural Science Museum]. In 1919, it became a <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">history</a> museum. Reflecting the architectural influence of the Versailles Palace in France, the Ipiranga's collection, with approximately 100,000 pieces, comprises works of art, furniture, clothing and appliances that belonged to those who took part in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brazil" title="History of Brazil">Brazilian history</a>, such as explorers, rulers and freedom fighters. Its facilities house a library with 100,000 books and the "Centro de Documentação Histórica", Historic Documentation Center, with 40,000 <a href="/wiki/Manuscript" title="Manuscript">manuscripts</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ema_Gordon_Klabin_Cultural_Foundation" title="Ema Gordon Klabin Cultural Foundation">Ema Gordon Klabin Cultural Foundation</a> opened to the public in March 2007. Its headquarters is a 1920s mansion. It houses 1545 works, including paintings by <a href="/wiki/Marc_Chagall" title="Marc Chagall">Marc Chagall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pompeo_Batoni" title="Pompeo Batoni">Pompeo Batoni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Gobert" title="Pierre Gobert">Pierre Gobert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frans_Post" title="Frans Post">Frans Post</a>, Brazilian modernists <a href="/wiki/Tarsila_do_Amaral" title="Tarsila do Amaral">Tarsila do Amaral</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Di_Cavalcanti" title="Di Cavalcanti">Di Cavalcanti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Candido_Portinari" title="Candido Portinari">Portinari</a>, period furniture, decorative and archeological pieces.
</p><p>Stretching over 78 thousand square meters (0.84 million square feet), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorial_da_Am%C3%A9rica_Latina" title="Memorial da América Latina">Memorial da América Latina</a> (<i>Latin America's Memorial</i>) was conceived to showcase <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin American countries</a> and their roots and cultures. It is home to the headquarters of Parlamento Latino-Americano – Parlatino (Latin American Parliament). Designed by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Niemeyer" title="Oscar Niemeyer">Oscar Niemeyer</a>, Memorial has an exhibition pavilion with permanent exhibition of the continent's craftwork production; a library with books, newspapers, magazines, videos, films and records about the history of Latin America; and a 1,679-seat auditorium.
</p><p>Hospedaria do Imigrante (<i>Immigrant's Hostel</i>) was built in 1886 and opened in 1887. Immigrant's Hostel was built in Brás to welcome the immigrants who arrived in Brazil through the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Santos" title="Port of Santos">Port of Santos</a>, quarantining those who were sick and helping new arrivals to find work in coffee plantations in Western, Northern and Southwestern São Paulo State and Northern Paraná State. From 1882 to 1978, 2.5 million immigrants of more than 60 nationalities and ethnicities were guests there,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hospedaria_dos_Imigrantes_1885_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hospedaria_dos_Imigrantes_1885-209">[209]</a></sup> all of them duly registered in the museum's books and lists. The hostel hosted approximately 3,000 people on average, but occasionally reached 8,000. The hostel received the last immigrants in 1978.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1998 the hostel became a museum, where it preserves the immigrants' documentation, memory and objects. Located in one of the few remaining centenarian buildings, the museum occupies part of the former hostel. The museum also restores wooden train wagons from the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Railway" title="São Paulo Railway">São Paulo Railway</a>. Two restored wagons inhabit the museum. One dates from 1914, while a second class passenger car dates from 1931. The museum records the names of all immigrants who were hosted there from 1888 to 1978.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Museum_of_Art" title="São Paulo Museum of Art">MASP</a> has one of world's most important collections of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_art_history" title="Western art history">European art</a>. The most important collections cover Italian and French painting schools. The museum was founded by <a href="/wiki/Assis_Chateaubriand" title="Assis Chateaubriand">Assis Chateaubriand</a> and is directed by <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Maria_Bardi" title="Pietro Maria Bardi">Pietro Maria Bardi</a>. Its headquarters, opened in 1968, were designed by <a href="/wiki/Lina_Bo_Bardi" title="Lina Bo Bardi">Lina Bo Bardi</a>. MASP organizes temporary exhibitions in special areas. Brazilian and international exhibitions of <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Photography" title="Photography">photography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Design" title="Design">design</a> and <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a> take turn during the whole year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup>
</p><p>Located next to the Luz metro station, the <a href="/wiki/Pinacoteca_do_Estado_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Pinacoteca do Estado de São Paulo">Pinacoteca do Estado de São Paulo</a> was projected by architect <a href="/wiki/Ramos_de_Azevedo" title="Ramos de Azevedo">Ramos de Azevedo</a> in 1895. It was constructed to house an Arts Lyceum. In 1911, it became a museum, where it hosts a number of art exhibitions, such as bronze statues of French sculptor <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Rodin" title="Auguste Rodin">Auguste Rodin</a> took place in 2001. There is also a permanent exhibition on the "Resistance" movement that took place during military dictatorship in the Republican period, including a reconstructed prison cell where political prisoners were kept.
</p><p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Oca_do_Ibirapuera&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Oca do Ibirapuera (page does not exist)">Oca</a> (<i>oca</i> means thatched house in Native Brazilian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tupi-Guarani_languages" title="Tupi-Guarani languages">Tupi-Guarani</a>) is a white, spaceship-like building sitting in the greens of <a href="/wiki/Ibirapuera_Park" title="Ibirapuera Park">Ibirapuera Park</a>. An exhibition place with more than 10 thousand square meters (0.11 million square feet). Modern art, Native Brazilian art, and photographie are some of the topics of past thematic exhibitions.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Museum_of_Image_and_Sound" title="São Paulo Museum of Image and Sound">Museu da Imagem e do Som</a> (<i>Image and Sound Museum</i>) preserves music, cinema, photography and <a href="/wiki/Graphic_design" title="Graphic design">graphical</a> arts. MIS has a collection of more than 200,000 images. It has more than 1,600 fiction videotapes, documentaries and music and 12,750 titles recorded in <a href="/wiki/Super_8_film" title="Super 8 film">Super 8</a> and 16 mm film. MIS organizes concerts, cinema and video festivals and photography and graphical arts exhibitions.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Art_of_the_Parliament_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Museum of Art of the Parliament of São Paulo">Museum of Art of the Parliament of São Paulo</a> is a contemporary art museum housed in the Palácio 9 de Julho, the Legislative Assembly of São Paulo house. The museum is run by the Department of Artistic Heritage of the Legislative Assembly and has paintings, sculpture, prints, ceramics and photographs, exploring the Brazilian contemporary art. 
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Football_Museum" title="Football Museum">Museu do Futebol</a> (<i>Football Museum</i>) is at the famous soccer stadium Paulo Machado de Carvalho, which was built in 1940 during Getúlio Vargas presidency. The museum shows the history of soccer with a special attention to the memories, emotions and cultural values promoted by the sport during the 20th and 21st centuries in Brazil. The visit also includes fun and interactive activities, 16 rooms from the permanent collection, plus a temporary exposition.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sede_de_O_Estado_de_Sao_Paulo_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="772" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Sede_de_O_Estado_de_Sao_Paulo_01.jpg/220px-Sede_de_O_Estado_de_Sao_Paulo_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Sede_de_O_Estado_de_Sao_Paulo_01.jpg/330px-Sede_de_O_Estado_de_Sao_Paulo_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Sede_de_O_Estado_de_Sao_Paulo_01.jpg/440px-Sede_de_O_Estado_de_Sao_Paulo_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sede_de_O_Estado_de_Sao_Paulo_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Headquarters of the newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/O_Estado_de_S._Paulo" title="O Estado de S. Paulo">O Estado de S. Paulo</a></i> on the <a href="/wiki/Marginal_Tiet%C3%AA" title="Marginal Tietê">Marginal Tietê</a></div></div></div>
<p>São Paulo is home to the two most important daily newspapers in Brazil, <i><a href="/wiki/Folha_de_S.Paulo" title="Folha de S.Paulo">Folha de S.Paulo</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/O_Estado_de_S._Paulo" title="O Estado de S. Paulo">O Estado de S. Paulo</a></i>. Also, the top three weekly news magazines of the country are based in the city, <i><a href="/wiki/Veja_(magazine)" title="Veja (magazine)">Veja</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%89poca_(Brazilian_magazine)" title="Época (Brazilian magazine)">Época</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISTO%C3%89" title="ISTOÉ">ISTOÉ</a></i>.
</p><p>Two of the five major television networks are based in the city, <a href="/wiki/Rede_Bandeirantes" title="Rede Bandeirantes">Band</a> and <a href="/wiki/RecordTV" title="RecordTV">RecordTV</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Sistema_Brasileiro_de_Televis%C3%A3o" title="Sistema Brasileiro de Televisão">SBT</a> and <a href="/wiki/RedeTV!" title="RedeTV!">RedeTV!</a> are based in <a href="/wiki/Osasco" title="Osasco">Osasco</a>, a city in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater São Paulo">São Paulo metropolitan area</a>, while <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rede_Globo" title="Rede Globo">Globo</a>, the country's most watched TV channel, has a major news bureau and entertainment production center in the city. In addition, <a href="/wiki/TV_Gazeta" title="TV Gazeta">Gazeta</a> is at <a href="/wiki/Paulista_Avenue" title="Paulista Avenue">Paulista Avenue</a> and the city is used for its station idents since 2014.
</p><p>Many of the major AM and FM radio networks of Brazil are headquartered in São Paulo, such as <a href="/wiki/Jovem_Pan" title="Jovem Pan">Jovem Pan</a>, Rádio Mix, <a href="/wiki/Transam%C3%A9rica_Pop" title="Transamérica Pop">Transamérica</a>, <a href="/wiki/BandNews_FM" title="BandNews FM">BandNews FM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Brasileira_de_Not%C3%ADcias" title="Central Brasileira de Notícias">CBN</a>, 89 A Radio Rock, Kiss FM and <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Bandeirantes_de_Comunica%C3%A7%C3%A3o" title="Grupo Bandeirantes de Comunicação">Band FM</a>. The telephone area code for the city of São Paulo is 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Paulo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Brazil" title="Sport in Brazil">Sport in Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Paulista" title="Campeonato Paulista">Campeonato Paulista</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aut%C3%B3dromo_Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Pace,_July_3,_2018_SkySat_(cropped_2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1608" data-file-width="2018" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Pace%2C_July_3%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped_2%29.jpg/220px-Aut%C3%B3dromo_Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Pace%2C_July_3%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped_2%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Pace%2C_July_3%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped_2%29.jpg/330px-Aut%C3%B3dromo_Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Pace%2C_July_3%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped_2%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Pace%2C_July_3%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped_2%29.jpg/440px-Aut%C3%B3dromo_Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Pace%2C_July_3%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped_2%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aut%C3%B3dromo_Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Pace,_July_3,_2018_SkySat_(cropped_2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Grand_Prix" title="São Paulo Grand Prix">São Paulo Grand Prix</a> is held at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Pace" title="Autódromo José Carlos Pace">Autódromo José Carlos Pace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Interlagos" title="Interlagos">Interlagos</a></div></div></div>
<p>The city hosts sporting events of national and international importance, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Grand_Prix" title="São Paulo Grand Prix">São Paulo Grand Prix</a>, held at the <a href="/wiki/Interlagos_Circuit" title="Interlagos Circuit">Interlagos Circuit</a>. Among the main events that São Paulo hosted are the <a href="/wiki/1950_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1950 FIFA World Cup">1950 FIFA World Cup</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1963_Pan_American_Games" title="1963 Pan American Games">1963 Pan American Games</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2000_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2000 FIFA Club World Championship">2000 FIFA Club World Championship</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a> <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_opening_ceremony" title="2014 FIFA World Cup opening ceremony">Opening Ceremony</a> (and five more matches from the same tournament) and The city also has a <a href="/wiki/Jockey_Club" title="Jockey Club">Jockey Club</a>, where the first race took place on October 29, 1876.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup>
</p><p>As in the rest of Brazil, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> is the most popular sport. The city's major teams are <a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Corinthians_Paulista" title="Sport Club Corinthians Paulista">Corinthians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sociedade_Esportiva_Palmeiras" title="Sociedade Esportiva Palmeiras">Palmeiras</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC" title="São Paulo FC">São Paulo</a>. <a href="/wiki/Associa%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Portuguesa_de_Desportos" title="Associação Portuguesa de Desportos">Portuguesa</a> is a medium club and <a href="/wiki/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Juventus" title="Clube Atlético Juventus">Juventus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nacional_Atl%C3%A9tico_Clube_(SP)" title="Nacional Atlético Clube (SP)">Nacional</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barcelona_Esportivo_Capela" title="Barcelona Esportivo Capela">Barcelona EC</a> are three small clubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> is also one of the most popular sports in Brazil. One of Brazil's most famous sportsmen is three-time Formula One world champion and São Paulo native <a href="/wiki/Ayrton_Senna" title="Ayrton Senna">Ayrton Senna</a>. The Formula One <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Grand_Prix" title="São Paulo Grand Prix">São Paulo Grand Prix</a> (formally known as the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="Brazilian Grand Prix">Brazilian Grand Prix</a>) is held at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Jos%C3%A9_Carlos_Pace" title="Autódromo José Carlos Pace">Autódromo José Carlos Pace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Interlagos" title="Interlagos">Interlagos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Socorro_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Socorro (district of São Paulo)">Socorro</a>. The Grand Prix has been held at the Interlagos circuit from <a href="/wiki/1973_Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="1973 Brazilian Grand Prix">1973</a> to 1977, in 1979 and 1980, and from <a href="/wiki/1990_Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="1990 Brazilian Grand Prix">1990</a> to the present. Four Brazilian drivers have won the Brazilian Grand Prix, all of whom were born in São Paulo: <a href="/wiki/Emerson_Fittipaldi" title="Emerson Fittipaldi">Emerson Fittipaldi</a> (<a href="/wiki/1973_Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="1973 Brazilian Grand Prix">1973</a> and <a href="/wiki/1974_Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="1974 Brazilian Grand Prix">1974</a>), <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Pace" title="Carlos Pace">José Carlos Pace</a> (<a href="/wiki/1975_Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="1975 Brazilian Grand Prix">1975</a>), <a href="/wiki/Ayrton_Senna" title="Ayrton Senna">Ayrton Senna</a> (<a href="/wiki/1991_Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="1991 Brazilian Grand Prix">1991</a> and <a href="/wiki/1993_Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="1993 Brazilian Grand Prix">1993</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Massa" title="Felipe Massa">Felipe Massa</a> (<a href="/wiki/2006_Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="2006 Brazilian Grand Prix">2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/2008_Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="2008 Brazilian Grand Prix">2008</a>). In <a href="/wiki/2007_Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="2007 Brazilian Grand Prix">2007</a>, a new local railway station <i>Autódromo</i> of the Line C (Line 9) of <a href="/wiki/Companhia_Paulista_de_Trens_Metropolitanos" title="Companhia Paulista de Trens Metropolitanos">CPTM</a>, was constructed near the circuit to improve access.
</p><p>Volleyball, basketball, skateboard and tennis are other major sports. There are several traditional <a href="/wiki/Sports_club" title="Sports club">sports clubs</a> in São Paulo that are home for teams in many championships. The most important are <a href="/wiki/Esporte_Clube_Pinheiros" title="Esporte Clube Pinheiros">Esporte Clube Pinheiros</a> (waterpolo, <a href="/wiki/Esporte_Clube_Pinheiros_(women%27s_volleyball)" title="Esporte Clube Pinheiros (women's volleyball)">women's volleyball</a>, swimming, <a href="/wiki/Esporte_Clube_Pinheiros_(basketball)" title="Esporte Clube Pinheiros (basketball)">men's basketball</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">handball</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clube_Athletico_Paulistano_(basketball)" title="Clube Athletico Paulistano (basketball)">Clube Athletico Paulistano (basketball)</a>, Esporte Clube Banespa (volleyball, handball and <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esporte_Clube_S%C3%ADrio_(basketball)" title="Esporte Clube Sírio (basketball)">Esporte Clube Sírio (basketball)</a>, Associação Atlética Hebraica (basketball), Clube Atlético Monte Líbano (basketball), Clube de Campo Associação Atlética Guapira (amateur football) and Clube Atlético Ipiranga (multi-sports and former professional football). 
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Corrida_S%C3%A3o_Silvestre_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1536" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Corrida_S%C3%A3o_Silvestre_2012.jpg/220px-Corrida_S%C3%A3o_Silvestre_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Corrida_S%C3%A3o_Silvestre_2012.jpg/330px-Corrida_S%C3%A3o_Silvestre_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Corrida_S%C3%A3o_Silvestre_2012.jpg/440px-Corrida_S%C3%A3o_Silvestre_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Corrida_S%C3%A3o_Silvestre_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Saint_Silvester_Road_Race" title="Saint Silvester Road Race">Saint Silvester Road Race</a> in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Saint_Silvester_Road_Race" title="Saint Silvester Road Race">São Silvestre</a> Race takes place every New Year's Eve. It was first held in 1925, when the competitors ran about 8,000 meters (26,000 feet). Since then, the distance raced varied, but is now set at 15 km (9.3 mi). The <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Indy_300" title="São Paulo Indy 300">São Paulo Indy 300</a> was an <a href="/wiki/IndyCar_Series" title="IndyCar Series">IndyCar Series</a> race in <a href="/wiki/Santana_(district_of_S%C3%A3o_Paulo)" title="Santana (district of São Paulo)">Santana</a> that ran annually from 2010 to 2013. The event was removed from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014_IndyCar_Series_season" title="2014 IndyCar Series season">2014 season</a> calendar. São Paulo hosted the official <a href="/wiki/1984_Tournament_of_the_Americas" title="1984 Tournament of the Americas">1984 Tournament of the Americas</a> (basketball) where the <a href="/wiki/Brazil_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Brazil men's national basketball team">Brazilian national team</a> won its first out of four gold medals.
</p><p>In Bom Retiro district, there is a public baseball stadium, Estádio Mie Nishi, while Santo Amaro district is the seat of the Núcleo de Alto Rendimento (NAR) is a high performance sports center focused on Olympic athletes. São Paulo is also <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>'s stronghold in Brazil, with the main rugby field in the city being at the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_Athletic_Club" title="São Paulo Athletic Club">São Paulo Athletic Club</a>, São Paulo's oldest club, founded by the British community.
</p><p>The city has five major stadiums: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morumbi_Stadium" title="Morumbi Stadium">Morumbi Stadium</a>, owned by <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC" title="São Paulo FC">São Paulo FC</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pacaembu_Stadium" title="Pacaembu Stadium">Pacaembu Stadium</a>, owned by the municipal administration;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Parque" title="Allianz Parque">Allianz Parque</a> arena by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S.E._Palmeiras" title="S.E. Palmeiras">S.E. Palmeiras</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arena_-_Allianz_Parque_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arena_-_Allianz_Parque-218">[218]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canind%C3%A9_Stadium" title="Canindé Stadium">Canindé Stadium</a>, owned by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguesa_de_Desportos" title="Portuguesa de Desportos">Portuguesa de Desportos</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbfstadium_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbfstadium-219">[219]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Arena_Corinthians" title="Arena Corinthians">Arena Corinthians</a>, owned by <a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Corinthians_Paulista" title="Sport Club Corinthians Paulista">Sport Club Corinthians Paulista</a>, located in <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Itaquera" title="Itaquera">Itaquera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FifaHost_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FifaHost-220">[220]</a></sup> It also has several volleyball and basketball gyms, tennis courts, and many other sports arenas, such as the <a href="/wiki/Gin%C3%A1sio_do_Ibirapuera" title="Ginásio do Ibirapuera">Ginásio do Ibirapuera</a>, intended mainly for athletics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ginásio_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ginásio-221">[221]</a></sup>
</p>
